Shorter cycles compound faster. This is why the static plan is correct (no re-planning mid-Act slows the cycle) and why sub-agent parallelism matters (compress Act duration). Every architectural decision that adds latency to the cycle needs to justify itself against this principle.

**Sequential search framing (AlphaGo structure):** The Orchestrator faces a sequential decision problem isomorphic with AlphaGo's:

| AlphaGo | Orchestrator |
|---------|-------------|
| Board position | Current project snapshot |
| Moves | Loop selections from the Loop Library |
| Win condition | Dream State complete |
| Policy network | Decide's loop selection (probability distribution over next loops) |
| Value network | Orient's confidence estimate (expected progress from current state) |
| MCTS rollouts | Fast-fail parallel probes (cheap exploration before committing to expensive full loops) |

Three architectural implications: (1) loop selection is a search problem, not a lookup — the Loop Library is the action space and the right move depends on position; (2) fast-fail parallel probes are MCTS rollouts — cheap simulations to estimate position value before committing to full loop execution, making the research directive format (exploration space + single metric + time budget) a rollout spec; (3) the long-term direction for Decide is a learned policy — currently deterministic rule-based selection, eventually a probability distribution over loops that improves through accumulated cycles. The calibration service accumulates the training signal. This is what "earn lightweight literal RL" means made concrete: not abstract policy gradients, but a policy network over the Loop Library action space trained on cycle outcomes.

**Implicit guidance and control (mature system property):** Boyd's diagram shows arrows bypassing Decide — from Orient directly to Act. Experienced operators skip the explicit Decide step when orientation is so well-calibrated that the right action is obvious. In the mature Orchestrator: a rich Loop Library + well-calibrated Orient means Decide becomes increasingly mechanical, eventually near-automatic. The system earns implicit guidance through accumulated loop execution and calibration. This is what compound learning looks like at the OODA level — not faster Decide, but Decide becoming unnecessary for familiar situations.

**Project hierarchy and sub-project scope:** Three levels:

| Level | Scope | Executed by |
|-------|-------|-------------|
| **Project** | decomposes into sub-projects; takes multiple OODA cycles | — |
| **Sub-project** | intended scope of one OODA cycle; Decide designs the task board around completing it | one OODA cycle |
| **Loop task** | one loop (code loop, eval loop) | one ephemeral sub-agent |

The sub-project is the right granularity for OODA scope — large enough to be meaningful, small enough to be completable. This mirrors the D-tier module note in the Capability Tiers: the D-tier module is the natural atomic unit for a single code loop run; the sub-project is the natural atomic unit for a single OODA cycle. Both levels are worth naming explicitly.

The sub-project is the cycle's mission, designated before the cycle begins (from the previous cycle's output, from the project's initial plan, or from explicit user input at the cycle boundary). Observe measures cycle-over-cycle: did we close the sub-project? If not, what remains? Orient routes accordingly — "finish it" or "continue toward it." Decide re-scopes to whatever remains open.

A sub-project may take more than one OODA cycle to complete; it is always *scoped for* one. Multiple cycles on the same sub-project is normal, not failure — it is the OODA loop doing its job. The sub-project as a unit persists until closed.

**Backwards inference (when no sub-project is designated):** Observe does not assume a sub-project exists. If none is designated, it works backwards: project exists with a plan → derive the next incomplete sub-project from it. Project exists without a complete plan → sub-project is completing the project definition. Nothing exists → sub-project is project definition itself (triggers dream-protocol: the Observe session becomes the generative session). The first OODA cycle of a new project therefore converges on project definition without special-casing — it emerges naturally from backwards inference.

---

## Capabilities

> The resource sorting surface. Each capability is a named thing the system can do that a resource directly informs. Capabilities map to functions (how we build them) and modules (where we build them). Updated as resources are incorporated.
> Coverage: `○` untouched · `◑` touched · `●` well covered

### Observe
- `◑` **State reading** — loads all memory surfaces and execution state into a unified picture targeted at the designated sub-project. The agent never starts from zero. Layers are organized by temporal horizon — most durable to most current:

  | Layer | Memory surface | Horizon |
  |-------|---------------|---------|
  | **Soul** | Ecosystem CLAUDE.md — identity, axiomatic commitments, harness orientation; spans all orgs | Permanent (bilateral consent to change) |
  | **Self-awareness** | Self-awareness document — full self-model, architecture, design principles | Permanent (human review gate) |
  | **Capability map** | Knowledge graph — concept nodes, skill clusters, org-level axioms | Accumulated (updated by reflect-protocol) |
  | **Observe personalization** | MEMORY.md — collaborator patterns, protocol adaptation signals | Accumulated (cross-session) |
  | **Org context** | Org CLAUDE.md + DREAM-STATE (consumed as pair) — current state + desired state | Org-lifecycle |
  | **Project context** | Project CLAUDE.md — repo-specific stack, constraints, codebase context. Path-scoped rules (`.claude/rules/` with `paths:` frontmatter) provide per-module conventions that activate only when the navigator works with matching files — conditional context without bloating the main CLAUDE.md | Project-lifecycle |
  | **History** | Loop artifacts, execution state, git state | Cycle-level / current |
  | **Active persistent clones** | Shadow clones operating across cycle boundaries — schedule, health, last report, originating cycle | Cross-cycle / live |

  When no sub-project is designated, applies backwards inference to identify one (see Architecture section). Everything else in Observe depends on this. **If Decide or Act needs to fetch during execution, Observe was incomplete.** Persistent clone management is a standing Observe responsibility: surface all active persistent clones, their health metrics and quality scores, flag any that have degraded below threshold (demotion candidates), identify OODA-managed skills with stable quality across N cycles (graduation candidates), and detect orphaned persistent clones that no longer serve the current dream state. The persistent clone roster is part of every snapshot — Orient needs to know what's running autonomously to reason about the system's current posture.
- `○` **Codebase documentation generation** — produces structured, explorable documentation with diagrams (Mermaid) for any org or application within an org. Hierarchical: top-level overview → key areas → module-level detail → file-level specifics. Each level includes architecture diagrams expressing structure and relationships. Reference for feel and quality: Google's CodeWiki (codewiki.google) — explorable hierarchy, mermaid diagrams per section, progressive depth from overview to individual file descriptions. Serves the pilot, not the navigator — rendered for human eyes, not loaded into agent context. The knowledge graph provides the relationship data; this capability renders it as navigable documentation. Applicable to any codebase the navigator works on, not just the orchestrator itself.
- `◑` **Gap detection** — identifies what's missing, unclear, or contradictory relative to the sub-project's acceptance criteria. Flags gaps as first-class fields in the snapshot. A gap is not just "something missing" — it is an underrepresented connection between otherwise-connected concept clusters in the knowledge graph. Structurally visible: appears as a low-connectivity region between clusters. Highest-leverage gap = the connection that would bridge the most isolated regions. This definition makes gap detection algorithmic, not impressionistic.
- `◑` **Improvement measurement** — measures whether the system improved across cycles (More/Better/New); structurally the reward function. See RL framing note. **Heat map / vestigial detection:** tracks actual file and skill usage patterns across executions, not assumed usage. Surfaces anti-patterns — skills that should be frequently used but aren't, vestigial elements that add noise without being accessed, gaps between what the system was designed to do and what it actually does. This is the diagnostic that drives Better (fix what's being used poorly), More (scale what's working), and New (what's entirely missing). Vestigial elements identified here are candidates for pruning, not just ignoring. **Sequential pattern mining:** heat map detection identifies what's being used; sequential pattern mining on temporal execution logs extends this to what sequence is being repeated. The system detects repeated action sequences across runs and automatically proposes skill creation candidates — making the "can we make this a skill?" closing question algorithmic rather than human-observed. A repeated sequence that isn't a skill yet is a gap; a skill that exists but is never sequenced is vestigial. Both are pruning signals. **Pruning pass:** improvement measurement is also when Observe runs a pruning pass — three targets: (1) ephemeral artifacts past their retention threshold (loop outputs superseded by newer runs, intermediate work products no longer referenced); (2) architectural drift (deprecated patterns appearing in recently modified code, stale documentation diverging from implementation, orphaned skills defined but never invoked); (3) compaction candidates (large state blobs that should be compressed to summaries + references). Pruning output feeds directly into Better (fix drift) and removal (remove vestigial). Not a separate agent or module — a named pass within `measure-improvement`.
- `◑` **Idea extraction** — structures raw multi-modal input (voice, images, documents, code, text) into workable context. First-class multi-modality.
- `○` **Research** — gathers external information the system doesn't already have. Triggers: new dependency, unfamiliar domain, API changes, technology evaluation, unexplored territory. Depth scales with need: single-page fetch for a quick API reference, structured doc site crawling for a new framework, comprehensive domain survey for unexplored territory. Findings are structured for Orient to consume — not raw pages, but synthesized knowledge with source attribution. Research is what makes "if Decide or Act needs to fetch during execution, Observe was incomplete" achievable in practice. Without research, Orient works with stale or incomplete information. Connects to domain verifiability: unexplored domains need research before they can be characterized as self-verifiable or not.
- `◑` **Snapshot synthesis** — combines all of the above into one unambiguous output for Orient. The only Observe output; the interface contract. Quality criterion: **falsifiability**. Every claim in the snapshot must be bounded and verifiable — categorizable as true or false. Not "the system is performing well" but "3 loops executed, 2 artifacts produced, 1 gate triggered, 4 capabilities untouched." Vague claims degrade Orient's ability to produce a specific path statement. The snapshot's falsifiability is the leading indicator of Orient quality downstream.

### Orient
- `○` **Situation triage** — classifies current situation type before applying frameworks. The meta-capability that coordinates all others.
- `◑` **Framework application** — applies sense-making frameworks (JTBD, coherence, patterns, knowledge graph) to transform the snapshot.
- `○` **Domain decomposition** — understands the sub-project's natural component structure: what are the components, what are the domain dependencies between them (as they exist in the problem, not the execution), which loop types are relevant to each component. This is structural understanding of the sub-project, not execution planning — Orient identifies *what* the sub-project is made of; Decide decides *how* to execute against it.
- `○` **Environment reduction** — makes the problem space smaller before solving. Almost always the highest-leverage first move.
- `○` **Path articulation** — produces the path statement Decide can act on without asking anything. The only Orient output; the interface contract with Decide. For a sub-project cycle, the path statement includes the domain decomposition: named components, domain dependencies, and relevant loop types per component. Structured form: a **problem constellation** — a center (the core problem all sub-problems relate to) plus N verifiable sub-problems plus their relationships (dependency, independence, shared constraints). Verifiability is the quality bar for decomposition: if a sub-problem cannot be stated as a falsifiable test, it has not been decomposed enough. Sub-problems are co-equal — no sub-problem is more fundamental than another; a sub-problem too large to carry a verifiable criterion becomes its own sub-project, not a deeper node. Decide receives the constellation and assigns each verifiable sub-problem to a loop; the verifiability criterion propagates as the loop spec's acceptance criterion and the self-eval rubric.
- `◑` **Knowledge formalization** — reflect-protocol handles at loop boundary (auto-triggered, mechanical promotion check). Orient does not make formalization decisions.

### Decide
- `○` **Loop assignment** — assigns loop types from the Loop Library to each domain component identified by Orient's decomposition. Each component-loop pairing becomes a task on the board. The Loop Library currently contains two active loops: eval loop, code loop. (Dream state generation belongs to Observe, not the Library.)
- `○` **Spec writing** — produces the spec for each loop task, calibrated exactly to what it needs to run without asking. Manages quality, latency, and throughput across the task board: which parallelism pattern (speed / multi-angle / fast-fail probes) applies to each task cluster, how to maximize throughput without sacrificing quality on critical-path tasks. Task granularity heuristic: smallest unit that produces a coherent, testable artifact. Finer-grained tasks give Act more parallelism levers; when uncertain, use finer granularity — the board accommodates more tasks more gracefully than under-specified large tasks. Lifecycle modifier: early sub-project tasks may be larger (architecture establishment, environment setup); mature sub-project tasks should be tight.
- `◑` **Dependency analysis** — derives the execution dependency graph from Orient's domain dependencies plus any additional execution constraints (e.g. a test loop that must follow an implementation loop). Mechanical translation, not inference.
- `○` **Plan production** — outputs the task board: loop tasks, specs, dependency graph, and acceptance criteria for the sub-project. The only Decide output; the interface contract with Act.

### Act
- `○` **Plan consumption** — reads and validates Decide's task board: a list of loop-level tasks with declared dependencies. Verifies all task specs are present and the dependency graph is acyclic before spawning anything.
- `◑` **Sub-agent spawning (when parallelism is earned)** — spawns ephemeral sub-agents for proven-independent tasks. The sub-agent executes its loop and terminates on completion. Not the default execution model — the primary agent executes tasks directly unless parallelism is justified by proven independence and low semantic coupling. **When sub-agents are used: minimal context AND minimal tool surface** — precise context injection (loop command + spec + relevant prior artifacts) plus tool whitelisting: sub-agents only have access to the MCP tools their task requires. These are orthogonal isolation dimensions — you can have full context and restricted tools. Principle of least privilege applied to the tool layer prevents a sub-agent from inadvertently calling tools outside its task scope. **Capability-based identity for ephemeral agents** — traditional RBAC assumes persistent principals; ephemeral agents need a different model. The tool whitelist is the capability grant: issued at spawn, expires at termination, no credential management required. The audit trail is the artifact chain: traceability comes from what the sub-agent produced and which task spawned it, not from persistent credentials. Scoped capabilities + artifact audit = the security model for agents that don't persist. **Sub-agent tool scoping** — sub-agents, when spawned, get scoped tool access via whitelisting. Depth constraint: sub-agents cannot spawn their own children. Prevents recursive explosion; parallelism is wide, not deep.
- `◑` **Task execution shapes and parallel coordination** — Decide specifies each task's execution shape in the task spec. Four task types, then four parallelism patterns within the parallel type:

  **Task types (execution shapes):**
  - **Atomic** — one agent, one pass, one result. The default for simple, well-understood tasks. No coordination overhead.
  - **Parallel** — N agents, independent portions of the work. Divisible tasks with no dependencies between portions. Uses the parallelism patterns below.
  - **Phased** — sequential steps with validation between each phase. For high-stakes or multi-step work where each phase depends on the last. The checkpoint between phases is a correctness gate, not a trust gate — the work requires sequential validation regardless of trust level.
  - **Competitive** — N agents attempt the same task independently, best result wins. For ambiguous tasks where approach matters more than execution. Structural implementation of deferred trust: trust the selection process, not individual agents. Decide specifies N, the comparison metric, and the selection mechanism.

  Manages concurrent execution via task board: tasks become claimable when their declared dependencies are satisfied, with no explicit phase layer between Act and sub-agents. Sub-agents claim and execute tasks concurrently up to the natural parallelism ceiling of the dependency graph. Sub-agents may surface new loop tasks to the board during execution — the board grows as work reveals new tasks, without triggering a replanning cycle. Four distinct parallelism patterns (apply within the parallel and competitive task types): (1) **speed parallelism** — independent loops running simultaneously because neither depends on the other's output; (2) **multi-angle coverage** — parallel agents attacking the same target from complementary directions (happy path + edge cases + validation; security + logic + regressions) — about thoroughness, not speed; (3) **fast-fail parallel probes** — many cheap experiments running in parallel, failing ones terminated early, successful ones allowed to run to completion. Economics: pay only for what succeeds, prune aggressively. Used in exploration under resource constraint (hyperparameter sweeps, approach validation). Fair comparison mechanism: fixed wall-clock time budget per probe — all probes run for the same duration, then compare on the single declared metric. This makes results comparable across probes with different architectures or approaches. (4) **stochastic consensus** — same query run N independent times, results aggregated by statistical weight. Exploits LLM stochasticity as a feature: consensus (majority agreement) = safe bets; divergences (split results) = context-dependent; outliers (1-2/N) = high-variance, potentially high-value ideas that never surface in a single run. Used at decision points with high uncertainty — Orient's `identify-path` when the highest-leverage gap is non-obvious, Decide's `select-loops` when loop selection is uncertain. The outlier category is the primary value: it surfaces non-obvious paths that single-run analysis systematically misses. Decide specifies which pattern applies and sets the time budget and metric; Act executes accordingly.
- `◑` **Amdahl's law as parallelism ceiling** — the speedup from parallel shadow clones is limited by the serial fraction of the OODA cycle (Amdahl, 1967). Serial phases: Observe, Orient, Decide, artifact collection, evaluation, compaction. Parallel phase: Act. If the serial fraction is 30% of total cycle time, maximum speedup is ~3.3x regardless of clone count. **Three implications for the harness:** (1) *Optimizing serial phases yields more total speedup than adding parallel capacity.* Making Observe faster (better context loading, leaner memory retrieval) or Decide leaner (faster planning) raises the ceiling for ALL parallelism. Going from 4 to 16 clones is marginal if serial phases dominate. (2) *Evaluation is the serial bottleneck of generation.* The generation-evaluation balance (encoded above) is Amdahl's law applied: N generators produce N results, but evaluation processes them serially. More generators without faster evaluation hits the wall. Invest proportionally in both. (3) *Compaction is a serial gate.* Every compaction event is serial overhead that bounds parallel throughput. The session memory template approach (pre-built summaries instead of forked summarizer) is an Amdahl optimization: reducing the serial fraction to raise the parallelism ceiling. **Decide should account for this:** diminishing returns on clone count are predictable from the serial fraction. The optimal N is where the marginal speedup from one more clone falls below the marginal cost (tokens, coordination overhead). Over-parallelization wastes resources for near-zero speedup.
- `○` **Artifact collection** — gathers and validates loop outputs against manifest declarations. Schema validation, not just file existence.
- `○` **Failure handling** — detects failures, records failure artifacts, surfaces to next Observe cycle. Guards against completion gaming: the failure mode where an agent declares victory prematurely, marks features done without verification, or removes tests to make them pass. Verification-before-completion is the harness-level response. Guards against **dirty handoff**: the failure mode where an agent leaves the environment broken or undocumented between sessions or phases — uncommitted changes, broken build, no progress notes, partial state that the next agent can't interpret. Distinct from completion gaming (false completion signals); dirty handoff is about the state of the ENVIRONMENT after the agent finishes, regardless of whether it claims success. Defense: each phase must commit, document progress, and leave the environment clean before yielding. The `create_handoff` tool exists for this; the failure mode names what happens when it's skipped. Guards against **orientation overhead**: the serial cost of re-reading context at the start of each fresh session. This is the tradeoff of context resets — you avoid compaction degradation but pay an orientation tax each iteration that scales with project history. Activity logs, progress files, and git history grow across iterations; late iterations spend significant context just figuring out where things stand before doing new work. This is Amdahl's law applied to the fresh context strategy: orientation is serial overhead. Defense: keep handoff artifacts lean (compressed summaries, not full logs), and design session memory templates that produce orientation-efficient summaries. **Never fix bad output — reset and fix the cause.** When an agent produces bad output, the correct response is not to patch the output but to diagnose the harness condition that caused it (bad spec, missing constraint, insufficient isolation), fix that, and rerun from scratch. Patching bad output accepts the debt and obscures the root cause; fixing the harness eliminates the failure mode for all future runs. This is the failure handling behavioral prescription: bad output is a harness diagnosis signal, not a repair target. **Escalate — the pattern for genuine failures and blockers.** Constraints are in-flow: Act adapts within spec, logs assumptions, queues new discoveries as task candidates, and continues. Escalation is reserved for failures and blockers where the task genuinely cannot proceed (dependency missing, upstream failure, unresolvable conflict) or where proceeding would be irreversible and outside declared scope. When escalating: record a typed blocker artifact (what failed, what decision is needed, what context is relevant), mark the task blocked, continue all other parallelizable work. The blocker artifact feeds the next Observe session as a first-class input — the voice surface resolves it with full context in minutes. Escalate is the mechanism that makes zero-gates a design reality: Act always has a path forward that doesn't require human interruption, and blockers travel upward to Observe rather than freezing execution.
- `◑` **Compaction** — preserves mission, decisions, constraints across cycle boundaries. Once per OODA cycle.
- `◑` **Cycle boundary signaling** — notifies that the cycle is complete and artifacts are ready for review; multi-modal output matched to context. **Notification layer: ntfy.sh** (replaces Slack — one curl call, zero OAuth, zero bot setup, free self-hostable service, app on iOS/Android). Proactive pattern: "I noticed ABC project needs XYZ — want me to proceed?" pushed as ntfy notification; user responds via voice surface rather than tapping buttons. **Interaction layer: voice surface** (custom STT→claude -p→TTS wrapper, see Observe module) — speak the response, full harness processes it, no screen required. ntfy handles the push; the voice surface handles the reply. Conservative fallback for high-stakes decisions: record decision artifact, surface at next Observe.

### Cross-cutting *(handling TBD)*
- `◑` **Memory and persistence** — Observe (reading) + Orient (formalizing) + Act (compaction)
- `◑` **Reinforcement learning** — Observe (reward function) + Orient (triage as future learned classifier); structurally equivalent now, earn lightweight literal
- `◑` **Multi-modality** — Observe (idea extraction inputs: voice, images, documents, code) + Act (gate/notification outputs: text, audio via voice surface, ntfy push). Output modality matches information type: text for reasoning, ASCII/Mermaid for spatial/relational state, audio for mobile contexts, generative video for milestone summaries. See Design Principles: *Output modality matches information type*.
- `◑` **Distributed systems patterns** — Act draws on distributed systems as a design language: write-ahead logging (persist state before acting), leader-follower (Orchestrator leads, sub-agents follow), optimistic execution (assume success, handle failure as information), horizontal scaling (parallel agents as the natural scaling unit). These aren't implementation choices — they're the conceptual vocabulary that makes Act's specific mechanisms (coordination state, atomic rename, two-layer WAL, parallel coordination) legible. Spans: Decide (dependency analysis, DAG) + Act (coordination, compaction, isolation).
- `○` **Agent coordination patterns** — sub-agent model, isolation, context injection

## Module Checklists

### Observe (pending)

**Purpose:** Read all persistent state, evaluate current outcomes, measure improvement, and produce a structured snapshot of where the system is — regardless of what the user brings to the table.

**Protocol library:** Observe selects from a library of self-contained protocols based on what the snapshot needs. The hard problem is selection: given what's missing or unknown, which protocol surfaces it? The library grows as the system encounters new context types. See protocol table in Design Context.

**Required Functions:**
- [ ] `surface-state` — read CLAUDE.md, loop artifacts, git history, and codebase structure (component relationships, architecture, source map) into a unified current state snapshot. Codebase structure is readable state — not just what has been decided about the code, but the actual shape of it.
- [ ] `select-protocols` — given the entry case and snapshot gaps, select the relevant protocols from the library and run them; no fixed order, selection is driven by what's missing
- [ ] `eval-outcomes` — run scenario tests against current system; measure outcome vs. desired outcome gaps. Include adversarial cases designed to find the failure boundary, not just confirm the working case — a capability assessment that only tests success reports an optimistic ceiling; one that finds the failure mode reports the actual one. The failure boundary is where the next design begins.
- [ ] `parse-ideas` — extract and structure raw multi-modal user input (voice, images, documents, code, rough text) into workable context when no spec exists; multi-modality is first-class here
- [ ] `parse-spec` — read and validate a spec (complete, incomplete, or in-progress); identify gaps
- [ ] `measure-improvement` — apply the More/Better/New framework symmetrically across all four capability primitives (protocols, frameworks, skills, evals): for each type, which should increase in volume, which should iterate, which are missing entirely; prioritized in that order. topology-protocol's gap output is the primary input — it surfaces gaps across all four types in a single pass over the knowledge graph. pattern-protocol, heat-protocol, and coherence-protocol supply additional improvement signals. Synthesis across all inputs produces the prioritized improvement list.
- [ ] `produce-snapshot` — output the structured current state snapshot for Orient. Every claim must be falsifiable — bounded, verifiable, categorizable as true or false. Not "the system is performing well" but "3 loops executed, 2 artifacts produced, 1 gate triggered." Vague claims degrade Orient's path statement; the snapshot's falsifiability is the leading indicator of cycle quality downstream.

**1% improvement:** Each Observe cycle measures whether the system improved by ~1% — via volume (More), quality (Better), or creation (New) across all four capability primitives: protocols, frameworks, skills, and evals. Skill harvesting and versioning are the primary mechanisms; the same dynamics apply to each primitive type.

**Six mechanisms for primitive evolution** — all four capability primitives (protocols, frameworks, skills, evals) can change through six distinct mechanisms, each with a different scope, trigger, and safety profile. All six apply universally to all four primitive types; some combinations are mature, others are frontier design work.

  | Mechanism | Scope | Trigger | Safety |
  |---|---|---|---|
  | **Manual editing** | Any change, any primitive | Human-initiated | Git versioning |
  | **Improvement queue** | Prose, parameters, configuration | End of loop + feedback | Proposal queue, human approval |
  | **Auto-calibration** | Numerical data (scores, estimates, thresholds) | Every completed phase | Bounded adjustment (±20%), exponential smoothing |
  | **Gap detection + drafting** | New primitives (additive only) | Pattern detection across N runs | Additive only, human approval |
  | **Semantic versioning + regression tests** | Primitive prose/logic | Improvement proposals | Semantic diff, test against rubric, auto-apply if passes / human review if uncertain |
  | **A/B variants** | Primitive execution | Continuous | Parallel execution, promote winner after N trials |

  The system should support all six simultaneously, routing each change to the appropriate mechanism based on scope. As trust builds, more changes flow through the autonomous mechanisms (auto-calibration, A/B variants) and fewer require the manual/queue path — earned autonomy applied to the improvement process itself.

**RL framing:** The More/Better/New framework is structurally equivalent to reinforcement learning — not purely metaphorical, not requiring actual training loops. Mapping: improvement measurement = reward function; skill versions + triage heuristics = policy; skill versioning + calibration feedback = policy update; More = exploitation; New = exploration. The calibration service and learning service are already the raw materials for lightweight literal RL (bandit-style: track which framework selections led to good path statements, bias future triage accordingly). Design principle: structurally equivalent now, earn lightweight literal. Do not implement policy gradients or value functions prematurely — the architecture already captures the RL structure; literal mechanisms layer on when the system is mature enough.

**Design Context:**
- **Parent/child agent split** — Observe operates at the Orchestrator (parent) level, not the implementing (child) level. It can run scenario tests the implementing sub-agent never saw. The evaluator is separated from the implementer by design — this is how evals stay honest.
- **Capability boundary probing** — knowing where a capability fails is part of knowing the capability. Scenario tests should include cases designed to find the failure boundary, not just confirm the working case. A capability assessment that only tests success reports an optimistic ceiling; one that finds the failure mode reports the actual one. Observe's scenario tests should include adversarial cases — inputs the sub-agent wasn't optimized for — to map the shape of the capability. Don't stop at "working." Probe until you find what breaks, because the failure boundary is where the next design begins.
- **Memory cycle entry point** — Observe is the reader and consolidator of the memory cycle: loop artifacts → reflect-protocol runs at loop boundary (CLAUDE.md updated, knowledge graph upserted, signals tagged) → cycle-level Observe reads consolidated state → snapshot → Orient synthesizes path statement. Dynamic state (artifacts) flows through reflect-protocol before it can become stable knowledge; by the time cycle-level Observe runs, CLAUDE.md already reflects completed loops.
- **The snapshot is the interface contract** — must be unambiguous regardless of entry case (ideas, complete spec, incomplete spec). Orient's ability to proceed without clarification depends entirely on snapshot quality.
- **U-shaped attention and the dumb zone** — LLM performance follows a U-shaped curve: highest when relevant information is at the beginning or end of context, significantly degraded in the middle — even in long-context models (Liu et al., TACL 2024). Three zones govern all context placement: (1) **static, foundational context at the beginning** (high attention zone 1) — identity, mission, constraints; (2) **nothing load-bearing in the middle** (low attention zone) — this is where context goes to die; (3) **freshly-retrieved, task-specific content at the end** (high attention zone 2) — current state, active decisions, recent artifacts. Two hard design rules follow: keep inputs small — push context beyond a certain threshold and signal-to-noise degrades, attention fragments, and errors that look like reasoning failures are actually information overload; freshly-retrieved information goes at the END to land in zone 2. The "large state → disk + summary" principle is the mechanism that keeps inputs out of the dumb zone. Progressive disclosure is not an optimization — it is the architecture required to stay out of it.
- **Large state → disk + summary** — any large state blob (accessibility tree, knowledge graph, full codebase, run archives) should be persisted to disk and only a summary + reference path injected into the snapshot. Never dump raw large state into context — it crowds out reasoning without adding proportional value. The CLI vs. MCP token difference (90k tokens for the same task) is the concrete proof. `surface-state` follows this rule: each source is summarized; the snapshot references artifacts, not their full content.
- **Entry case handling** — both "ideas in head" and "spec-driven" (with 3 sub-cases: complete, incomplete, rough draft) must produce the same consistent snapshot format. The format can't depend on what the user brought to the table.
- **Observe reads; loops create** — Observe reads what exists. Library loops (eval loop, code loop) create what doesn't exist yet. They are in a producer-consumer relationship: loops produce artifacts, Observe consumes them. Observe also generates the dream state artifact directly via dream-protocol — the one case where Observe creates rather than reads. Observe's reading mechanism never changes across cycles — it always reads what's there. The snapshot looks different each cycle because loops have been creating artifacts.
- **System context vs. domain context** — Observe gathers system context (what has been done, what artifacts exist, current state of the system). Context-gathering loops produce domain context (vision, bottlenecks, what needs to be built). Domain context becomes system context the moment it's written to an artifact — that's when Observe can read it. Observe doesn't need to understand what loops produce; it just reads all artifacts.

- **Project genesis signal — dual trigger:** new projects don't require upfront architecture; they emerge from two signals converging. (1) *Top-down intent declaration* — the human names the destination ("this cluster is eventually a daily ritual app"), which creates the attractor and gives accumulation somewhere to point. Without this, a dense resource cluster is shapeless — the signal is present but not directed. (2) *Bottom-up resource accumulation* — resources cluster around a domain; as cluster density grows, the cluster's shape implies what the project requires. Without this, the declared intent is ungrounded — a name without substance. When both are present, Observe surfaces a project genesis signal: the declared intent has enough resource mass to begin implying an architecture. Observe reads both signals: intent declarations from Dream State and CLAUDE.md; cluster density from the knowledge graph and inbox accumulation. **Automation vs. amplification — how the cluster shape determines architectural direction:** once genesis is triggered, the resource cluster itself signals what kind of system to build. Resources about process, execution, tracking, and optimization point toward *automation* — the tool does the capability for you, substituting Intelligence for Labor. Resources about practice, understanding, habit formation, and growth point toward *amplification* — the tool develops the capability in you, the human remains in the loop at execution time. A cluster can point at both simultaneously, producing a system with an automation layer and an amplification layer. Reading the cluster before architecting is the design move: the resources have already done the requirements work.

- **Existing orchestrator modules are Observe's implementation** — the 26 existing modules largely already do what Observe needs. They just aren't coordinated into a unified snapshot. Mapping: memory-service + dream-state-service + run-archival + knowledge-graph → `surface-state`; learning-service + calibration-service + coherence-system + scoring + analytics → `eval-outcomes`; inbox-processor + voice → `parse-ideas`; learning-service + mece-opportunity-mapping + scoring + patterns-roundup → `measure-improvement`. The genuine new work is `produce-snapshot` (synthesis layer) and `parse-spec` (spec validation).
- **Why loop essence work comes before Observe design** — Observe's snapshot format depends on what loops produce. The artifact reference files defined in each loop's essence work are the schema Observe reads from. You can't design the reader until you know what the writer writes.
- **Filesystem + code sandbox as modality substrate** — any input modality (images, audio, documents) lands on disk first, then code executes the extraction (OCR, transcription, bounding box detection, annotation). The agent loops: write to disk → execute extraction code → read back structured output → reason. No specialized modality pipeline required — the filesystem is the universal interface and the code sandbox is the universal transformer. `parse-ideas` follows this pattern for all modalities: images are files, audio transcripts are files, documents are files. This is the same "large state → disk + summary" principle applied at the intake layer: the raw modality never enters context directly; only the structured extract does. The filesystem + code pattern absorbs new modalities without new architectural components.
- **Indirect prompt injection boundary** — when Observe reads external content (web pages via Firecrawl, documents, external APIs), that content is untrusted data. A malicious document could contain injected instructions designed to hijack the agent. The architectural defense: external content is *data*; CLAUDE.md is *instructions*. Never inject external content directly into the reasoning context — it must go to disk first (bounded buffer, structured extraction), then only a summary or structured extract enters the snapshot. The "large state → disk + summary" principle is also the security boundary. Observe enforces this separation on every external read.
- **Assumption enumeration** — when parsing a spec or processing a new context, Observe explicitly enumerates operating assumptions and flags which ones are unfalsified. Not "here's the spec content" but "here's the spec content + here are the assumptions it's operating under + here are the ones we can't verify yet." Unfalsified assumptions that matter become the precise question Observe surfaces. This is the epistemological audit applied at intake: ruthlessly interrogating what is known vs. assumed before passing anything to Orient.
- **User as context source** — the user is one of Observe's sources, not a collaborator in the loop. Expensive (requires attention), irreplaceable (only they can provide certain things), and reliably under-tapped. Observe is the only phase that interfaces with the user; Orient, Decide, and Act work exclusively with what Observe surfaced. The ordering is economic: passive sources first (cheaper), user last (most expensive). Context saturation bias: default to drawing out more — the user signals when they are done, not Observe. Even when context seems complete, continued prompting reliably surfaces ideas, constraints, and clarity that no artifact could provide.
- **Conversational feel** — when passive sources are insufficient, Observe surfaces one precise question — not a checklist. The interaction should feel like talking to someone who has read everything and identified exactly what only the user can provide. Multiple questions signals a module architecture problem.
- **Steerable reading via priority configuration** — Observe can be directed by a lightweight configuration (analogous to DeepWiki's `wiki.json`) that specifies what to surface, what hierarchy matters, and what to prioritize. This is not contradicting "Observe reads; loops create" — it is the human saying "here's what's important" at the reading level, the same way CLAUDE.md says "here's what's important" at the conclusions level. CLAUDE.md = stable knowledge (what has been decided); priority config = reading direction (what to look at). Without this, Observe reads everything uniformly; with it, Observe reads with focus. The config is a first-class input to `surface-state`, not a runtime parameter. Two tiers of config: project-level (CLAUDE.md — applies to all loops) and loop-specific (analogous to REVIEW.md — always check X, skip Y, style Z; written by Decide as part of spec generation and injected by Act into the sub-agent's context). The loop-specific config does not live in Observe — it is produced by Decide and consumed by the sub-agent. Observe reads the project-level config only.

- **Voice Observe surface — self-contained mobile interface** — Observe is uniquely self-contained among the four phases: it has its own input channel (voice), its own runtime, its own output (snapshot → inbox), and operates independently of the full OODA loop. This makes it deployable as a standalone surface before Act is complete — you can run voice Observe sessions today and feed their snapshots into manual or semi-automated loops.

  The voice session architecture (confirmed working):
  ```
  Phone mic → STT (Whisper / Voxtral) → claude -p \
    --strict-mcp-config \
    --mcp-config '{"mcpServers":{"orchestrator":{"type":"http","url":"http://localhost:3002/mcp"}}}' \
    --continue --output-format stream-json \
  → TTS (ElevenLabs/OpenAI) → earbuds
  ```
  Full harness access confirmed: CLAUDE.md loaded from working directory, Orchestrator MCP tools available, built-in tools (Bash, Read, Write, Edit) unaffected by `--strict-mcp-config`. The flag prevents hanging on other user MCP configs; `--continue` maintains conversation state across turns. Build: ~400 LOC — voice endpoint in Orchestrator server (~150), STT bridge (~30), TTS bridge (~30), session manager (~20), PWA phone client (~150).

  **Local-first voice layer.** The STT+TTS layer can run entirely on consumer hardware — open-source models now match cloud quality at zero marginal cost and zero latency penalty from round-trip. **STT spectrum:** Whisper (transcription only, lightweight) → Voxtral (audio understanding + transcription, 4.7B Mini / 24.3B Small, Apache 2.0). Voxtral uses Whisper large-v3 as its encoder but adds an instruction-tuned Mistral decoder — a strict superset of Whisper's capabilities. Upgrade path: start with Whisper for basic voice commands, move to Voxtral when audio understanding matters (processing meetings, podcasts, voice notes for Observe ingestion, semantic analysis of spoken content). Voxtral handles up to 40 minutes of audio in a single pass (32K context, 12.5Hz effective frame rate after 4x downsampling). **TTS:** Mistral TTS or Qwen3-class TTS for synthesis. Cloud TTS (ElevenLabs/OpenAI) remains an option for voice quality preference, but it is not an architectural dependency. The voice surface is deployable with no external service contracts.

  **Nested topic mechanic (NotebookLM interactive podcast model):** the session maintains an explicit topic stack. Zoom-in: "let's go deeper on X" enters a sub-conversation on X with its own resolution. Climb-out: when X resolves, the conversation returns to the parent topic with X's synthesis as a new input. Each resolution feeds up. Final state: the stack flattens into a structured Observe snapshot. This is recursive OODA at the micro level — each sub-topic is its own mini observe-orient-decide cycle, resolving before returning to parent. It enables extended context-gathering sessions (car, gym) with genuine depth — not linear monologue but inception-style exploration.

  **Context by mobile scenario:**
  - *Driving:* async voice capture → inbox (safety constraint; real-time interaction not viable). Record structured voice memos framed as Observe inputs ("here's what I observed about X, here's the decision I'm wrestling with") — inbox processor handles them as first-class Observe artifacts at next session.
  - *Exercising:* live voice session via the voice surface — full recursive conversation with harness access, real-time TTS responses through earbuds.

  **Handoff:** at session end, Claude synthesizes the full topic stack into a structured Observe snapshot and POSTs to the Orchestrator inbox. The next Claude Code session processes the inbox and starts at Orient, not Observe. The voice session IS the Observe phase.

  *Session end trigger:* "end session" / "that's everything" / "wrap up" voice command triggers synthesis. Fallback: 90 seconds of silence auto-triggers. Both paths produce the same snapshot POST. The `--continue` flag scopes to one sitting — a new sitting starts a fresh `--continue` chain so sessions don't bleed into each other. Staleness check on initialization: if the most recent artifact or execution is older than 48 hours, the briefing flags it explicitly ("heads up — last loop ran 3 days ago, state may have drifted") rather than presenting stale state as current.

  **Observe as the only human-facing surface.** Orient, Decide, and Act are fully automated — machine-to-machine. The voice surface makes this architectural fact physical: the microphone is the boundary between human and machine. Everything on the human side of that boundary is intention, context, judgment, constraint. Everything on the machine side is execution.

  Two corollaries follow:

  *Gates are Observe failures — all of them.* Act is designed to be fully autonomous. Constraints are welcome in the flow of a loop — Act handles them in-flow: adapts within spec, logs assumptions, queues discoveries, continues. What cannot be handled in-flow are genuine **failures and blockers**: the task cannot proceed at all, or proceeding would be irreversible and outside declared scope. These are handled by **escalate** — Act records a typed blocker artifact, marks the task blocked, continues executing other parallelizable tasks, and the blocker surfaces in the next Observe session as a first-class input. Observe's success metric is zero gates. A system with zero gates is a system where Observe extracts everything upfront and Act knows when to escalate vs. adapt.

  *Observe investment has maximum downstream leverage.* Because all human judgment enters through Observe and nowhere else, improving voice session quality improves everything downstream simultaneously: better snapshot → better path → better execution → fewer gate interruptions → longer autonomous run time. The voice surface isn't a convenience feature — it is the primary leverage point in the entire architecture.

  **Snapshot schema** — the interface contract between Observe and Orient. Every field is falsifiable: concrete, bounded, verifiable. Vague fields propagate as Orient uncertainty; the snapshot is the precision budget for the entire cycle.

  ```
  ObserveSnapshot {
    sub_project: string             // designated target for this cycle
    state: {
      artifacts:  ArtifactRef[]    // loop outputs with staleness indicators
      executions: ExecutionSummary // recent cycles: what ran, completed, failed
      memory:     MemorySummary    // key decisions, patterns, calibration state
      codebase:   CodebaseSummary  // architecture, component map, recent changes
    }
    gaps: Gap[]                     // { description, severity, graph_location }
    improvement: {
      more:      SkillRef[]        // skills to run at higher volume
      better:    SkillRef[]        // skills to iterate
      new:       string[]          // capabilities entirely missing
      vestigial: SkillRef[]        // skills never invoked — pruning candidates
    }
    assumptions: Assumption[]       // { claim, falsified: bool, source }
    user_context: {
      intent:           string     // what the human wants this cycle
      constraints:      string[]   // hard constraints surfaced
      priorities:       string[]   // ordering signal
      voice_session_id?: string    // if sourced from voice session
    }
    system_context: {
      active_capabilities: SkillRef[]   // skills and loops currently in the library — prevents Orient/Decide recommending what already exists
      memory_surface_state: {           // last-written summary per surface — prevents redundant promotions
        project_claude_md: string       // digest of recent constraint additions
        dream_state:       string       // current sub-project status and open gaps
        knowledge_graph:   string       // recently added concept nodes
        memory_candidates_queue: number // pending candidates awaiting cycle-level processing
      }
    }
    open_questions:  string[]       // what Observe could not resolve — Orient determines uphill/downhill from this + gaps + assumptions directly
    schema_version:  string         // e.g. "1.0.0" — increment on any field addition or removal; Orient validates before consuming
    produced_at:     timestamp
  }
  ```

  **Snapshot as traversable graph (direction for v2)** — the current schema is a typed flat struct: fields read sequentially top to bottom. A more powerful form is a graph slice: nodes for active concerns (gaps, assumptions, open questions, key artifacts), edges for relationships and dependencies between them (this gap blocks that artifact, this assumption underlies that open question). Traversal from highest-connectivity nodes outward — rather than linear field-by-field parsing — gives Orient a naturally prioritized entry point: the most-connected concerns surface first, the peripheral ones trail. The relational structure between concerns carries as much information as the individual items. The struct form is the right starting point (simple, well-defined, immediately buildable). The graph form is the right destination (richer, traversable, self-prioritizing). Migration path: add an optional `relationships: Edge[]` field to the struct that links concern IDs — Orient can ignore it if absent, exploit it when present. The snapshot evolves from read-only to navigable without breaking the interface contract.

  **Comprehension debt** — as the system runs autonomously, a gap grows between human understanding and system state: code lands that wasn't written or overseen directly, decisions were made by agents the human never saw. This is a distinct failure mode from technical failures — the system may be working correctly while the human's mental model drifts. Left unaddressed, it compounds: the human can't make good decisions about what to build next if they don't know what already exists. The mitigation is the session initialization protocol: every Observe cycle opens with a full artifact digest before any new direction is set. Regular deep-dives (reading code, reviewing decisions) are the manual complement.

  **Session initialization protocol** — every voice session opens with an oriented briefing. The system arrives ready, not cold:
  1. Dream state summary: current phase, modules complete vs. remaining, momentum direction
  2. Last snapshot's open questions: what was unresolved, what Observe couldn't extract last time
  3. Recent artifact digest: what loops ran since last session, what they produced, what failed
  4. Gate queue: any Act decisions waiting for human input

  Opening line: *"Here's where we are: [dream state]. Since last session: [artifact digest]. I have [N] open questions from last time. What do you want to go into?"*

  The system arrives oriented so the human doesn't spend the first third of the session recalibrating Claude. They confirm, correct, or dive directly into a topic. Initialization quality is session efficiency.

  **Topic stack mechanic — system prompt design.** The stack is explicit, not implied. Two parallel representations: transcript (text) and audio (spoken). They carry the same information differently.

  *Transcript mode* — every Claude response begins with a bracket header showing current position:

  `[auth-service → token expiry decision]`

  *Audio mode* — the TTS layer strips bracket notation before synthesis. Claude instead announces navigation verbally as part of its natural response: "I'm going deeper on token expiry now, staying in the auth-service context..." on PUSH; "Okay, I think we've resolved token expiry — short-lived tokens with a refresh pattern. Coming back up to auth-service..." on POP. The verbal announcement is part of the response text, not a header — it reads naturally when spoken and provides the same orientation signal the bracket provides visually.

  Navigation is natural language — same commands work in both modes:
  - *"let's dig into that" / "go deeper on X"* → PUSH(X), carry relevant parent context down
  - *topic reaches natural resolution* → POP(), synthesize to 1–2 sentences, inject synthesis as new parent-level context
  - *"come back up"* → explicit POP()
  - *"how does this connect to the bigger picture?"* → peek at parent without popping

  System prompt invariants: (1) every response shows current stack position (bracket in transcript, verbal in audio); (2) on PUSH, carry relevant parent context down — "in the context of auth-service..."; (3) on POP, synthesize before returning — synthesis is not optional, it's the mechanism that makes the parent richer on return; (4) at session end, flatten the stack bottom-up — each leaf synthesis feeds into its parent recursively until the root is a complete Observe snapshot.

  The stack flattening IS snapshot generation — not a separate step. A session with N resolved topics automatically produces an N-field snapshot. The conversation and the output are the same artifact.

- **Observe protocol library:** Observe has a library of self-contained protocols. Each protocol is a complete procedure for surfacing a specific kind of context. Selection is based on what the snapshot needs — the entry case and context gaps determine which protocols are relevant. No fixed composition order; the library grows as the system learns new observation patterns. The hard problem is selection: given what's missing from the snapshot, which protocol fills it best? Each protocol mines a specific substrate for a specific resource — the `data_source` field in the manifest is the substrate; the snapshot contribution is the extracted resource. The library's MECE-ness is checkable by asking: are there substrates we're not mining? The protocol library defines the harness's umwelt — the boundary of what it can perceive.

  | Protocol | Substrate | Resource extracted |
  |----------|-----------|-------------------|
  | reflect-protocol | Loop artifacts | Memory-candidates → memory surfaces |
  | topology-protocol | Knowledge graph | Structural gaps across all four primitives |
  | pattern-protocol | Execution logs | Repeated sequences → skill candidates |
  | coherence-protocol | Documented vs. actual behavior | Drift signals |
  | heat-protocol | Invocation patterns | Vestigial/underperforming elements |
  | dream-protocol | Human intent | Vision, direction, constraints |
  | cbr-protocol | Run archives | Similar past cycles → adaptation notes |
  | ingestion-protocol | External resources | Concepts, insights → knowledge graph + memory surfaces |
  | research-protocol | External information landscape | Synthesized knowledge for unfamiliar domains, dependencies, and technologies |
  | exploration-protocol | Data resources (tabular, time series, structured) | Dataset characterization — distributional shape, hygiene, flagged anomalies, segment behavior |
  | structure-protocol | Data resources (high-dim or unlabeled) | Unsupervised structure — principal axes with variance explained, cluster assignments with three-check validation |
  | association-protocol | Data resources (multi-feature) | Pairwise and n-ary relationships — correlations, regression coefficients, mutual information, collinearity caveats |
  | temporal-protocol | Data resources (time-indexed) | Time decomposition — trend, seasonality, changepoints, current regime, autocorrelation structure |
  | inference-protocol | Data resources (as a sample from a population) | Population parameter estimates with uncertainty bounds, sampling quality audit, multiple-comparison correction |
  | causal-protocol | Data resources (observational or experimental) | Treatment effect estimates with identification assumptions explicitly named |
  | clone-protocol | Active persistent clones | Health status, graduation/demotion candidates, orphan detection |

  | Protocol | Description | Snapshot contribution |
  |----------|-------------|----------------------|
  | **reflect-protocol** | the memory-candidates pipeline; collects, validates, and routes candidates from completed loop artifacts to the six memory surfaces | queued candidates validated against formalization threshold (recurrence, non-obviousness, durability); routed by declared type; `architectural` type gates for human review; pattern/coherence/heat signals tagged for their protocols |
  | **topology-protocol** | reads the knowledge graph to surface structural gaps across all four capability primitives; reasons about node isolation, betweenness, and cluster density | skill gaps (concept nodes with no owning skill — unexecutable capabilities); eval gaps (no owning eval — unmeasured capabilities); protocol gaps (no owning protocol — context types with no surfacing procedure); framework gaps (no owning framework — domains with no reference structure); high-betweenness bridge concepts with no owning skill cluster (highest-leverage `New` targets); sparse clusters (underdeveloped capability areas) |
  | **pattern-protocol** | surfaces repeated sequences and volume signals across all four capability primitives | `improvement.more`; `improvement.new` candidates across all four primitive types (skills, evals, protocols, frameworks) |
  | **coherence-protocol** | surfaces drift between skills/loops and documented behavior | `gaps` flagged as architectural drift; `improvement.vestigial` |
  | **heat-protocol** | surfaces actual invocation patterns vs. designed invocation | `improvement.vestigial` (never-invoked); `improvement.better` (underperforming) |
  | **dream-protocol** | surfaces human intent, vision, constraints, direction via voice session | `user_context`; `open_questions`; `sub_project` designation |
  | **cbr-protocol** | surfaces the most similar past cycle — path, loops, outcome | historical cycle context enriching the snapshot |
  | **ingestion-protocol** | reads external resources (articles, videos, papers); Phase 1 harvests a MECE list of everything potentially interesting (no filtering); Phase 2 applies the triage rubric to the harvested list | `memory_candidates` routed by type: `concept` → knowledge graph (isolated concept nodes; gaps surfaced across all four primitive types — capability, measurement, observation, reference); `architectural` → self-awareness document (human review gate); `improvement.new` candidates |
  | **research-protocol** | gathers external information the system doesn't already have; triggers: new dependency, unfamiliar domain, API changes, technology evaluation, unexplored territory; depth scales with need (single-page fetch → structured doc site crawl → comprehensive domain survey); distinct from ingestion-protocol which processes known resources — research-protocol discovers and evaluates unknown ones | synthesized knowledge with source attribution for Orient to consume; domain verifiability assessment (self-verifiable, not self-verifiable, or unexplored); dependency documentation for Act's shadow clones at spawn time |
  | **exploration-protocol** | surveys the distributional shape of an ingested data resource before any modeling — hypothesis-free coverage. Runs distribution inspection (median/IQR preferred over mean/SD when skewed), hygiene checks (missingness pattern MCAR/MAR/MNAR, outliers, encoding anomalies, duplicates, unit and date-parsing sanity), pairwise relationships, and segmentation checks. Every claim is distribution-shape-aware: "trend X" is reported only if it survives robust re-description against the underlying distribution; plots-over-summary-stats is the rule (Anscombe's quartet). Guards against Simpson's paradox by always running the segment breakdown when reporting an aggregate | `dataset_characterization`: shape summary (distribution, central tendency, spread), hygiene report, flagged anomalies, segment-level behavior; explicit "can this data answer the question?" verdict as the primary output |
  | **structure-protocol** | runs dimensionality reduction (PCA / UMAP / t-SNE, with t-SNE distances flagged as non-metric) and clustering (k-means / HDBSCAN / GMM / hierarchical) on data resources. Enforces the three-check validation before any cluster assignment is written to the snapshot: (1) stability under resampling, (2) separation (silhouette or equivalent), (3) interpretability. Rejects clusters that fail any of the three — k-means will always return k clusters whether or not clusters exist, and the three-check is how the protocol refuses to ratify spurious structure. Standardization is mandatory before PCA; principal components are reported as "uninterpretable composites" unless a loadings interpretation earns the label | `structural_summary`: principal axes with variance explained and loadings, cluster assignments with validation scores; rejection log for structure candidates that failed the three-check |
  | **association-protocol** | computes pairwise and n-ary relationships across features of a data resource — correlation matrices, regression coefficients with standard errors, mutual information, partial correlation, collinearity (VIF) checks. Distinguishes association from causation explicitly: every output is labeled "correlation only, not effect under intervention" unless causal-protocol has independently established identification. Flags extrapolation risk when a relationship is queried outside the training range | `relationship_graph`: associations with strength, uncertainty, and collinearity caveats; explicit correlation-not-causation labeling; extrapolation-unsafe regions named |
  | **temporal-protocol** | decomposes time-indexed data into trend / seasonality / changepoints / residual. Runs autocorrelation analysis, regime detection, and stationarity checks. Reports the current regime explicitly so downstream reasoning knows whether a trend claim is a real change or a within-regime fluctuation. Peeked-inference guard: when continuous monitoring produces sequential claims, uses always-valid inference so repeated looks don't inflate false-positive rates | `temporal_decomposition`: trend component, seasonal cycles, detected changepoints with timestamps, current regime, autocorrelation structure; sequential-claim corrections when applicable |
  | **inference-protocol** | executes the sample-to-population pipeline: (1) audit sample quality (random / stratified / convenience / self-selected — quality dominates size), (2) compute the statistic, (3) quantify re-sampling variance (standard error via closed-form or bootstrap), (4) produce a probabilistic statement about the population parameter (confidence interval or Bayesian posterior). Applies multiple-comparison correction (Bonferroni / FDR) whenever more than one test is run. Reports effect size alongside any significance claim — statistical significance is never sufficient on its own. Sample-quality audit is load-bearing: a million-row convenience sample is reported as weaker than a thousand-row random one | `inferential_claims`: population parameter estimates with uncertainty bounds, sample-quality audit result, effect sizes, correction applied, explicit statement of what was assumed about the sampling procedure |
  | **causal-protocol** | estimates treatment effects under intervention using identification-first methods: difference-in-differences, regression discontinuity, instrumental variables, synthetic control, do-calculus. Identification assumptions are stated *before* any estimate is produced; when the assumptions cannot be stated or cannot be defended from the data and domain knowledge, the protocol returns "unidentified" rather than an estimate. Distinct from association-protocol: association reports P(Y\|X); causal-protocol reports P(Y\|do(X)) | `causal_claims`: treatment effect estimates with identification assumptions explicitly named and defended; "unidentified" verdicts when assumptions cannot be made; sensitivity analysis for assumptions that can be relaxed |
  | **clone-protocol** | surfaces the state of all active persistent shadow clones — health metrics, quality scores, schedule adherence, resource consumption, last report timestamp, originating cycle. Five responsibilities: (1) **roster** — enumerate all active persistent clones with current status; (2) **health check** — flag any clone whose quality has degraded below its declared threshold (demotion candidate); (3) **graduation scan** — identify OODA-managed skills with stable quality across N+ cycles that are candidates for promotion to persistent clone; (4) **orphan detection** — find persistent clones whose originating purpose no longer serves the current dream state or whose spawning cycle's goals have been superseded; (5) **event collection** — gather events injected by persistent clones since the last Observe cycle and include them in the snapshot for Orient. Clone-protocol runs automatically at each cycle-level Observe invocation alongside reflect-protocol — it is not on-demand because persistent clone health is always relevant | `persistent_clone_roster` (active clones with health); `demotion_candidates` (degraded clones); `graduation_candidates` (mature OODA-managed skills); `orphaned_clones` (no longer serving dream state); `clone_events` (events injected since last cycle) |

  CBR-protocol's **Retain** step happens at cycle completion: Act's run archival writes the adapted case back to the archive, closing the loop. dream-protocol is the most intensive flavor — the extended voice session for vision generation. All protocols are Observe; none are Loop Library entries. The library grows over time: new protocols are added when new context types emerge that existing protocols don't surface.

  **reflect-protocol** is the exception to on-demand selection: it runs automatically at each loop completion (hooked to Act's loop boundary) and always runs first when cycle-level Observe is invoked. It is the memory-candidates pipeline — the complete internal path from loop artifact to memory surface.

  **Two-stage operation:**

  *Stage 1 — Collect (loop boundary, automatic):* reads `memory_candidates` frontmatter from the completed artifact and appends each candidate to the memory-candidates queue. No promotion yet. Knowledge graph concept nodes and edges to all four primitive types are upserted immediately (these are structural facts, not candidates requiring curation). Coherence and heat signals are tagged inline for their respective protocols.

  *Stage 2 — Process (cycle-level Observe, runs first):* processes the full queue as a batch, enabling cross-artifact recurrence detection. For each candidate: (1) validate routing type is correctly declared; (2) apply formalization threshold — recurrence (appeared in 2+ artifacts independently), non-obviousness (not immediately inferrable), durability (architectural not tactical); (3) candidates that pass route to their declared surface; (4) `architectural` type always gates for human review regardless of threshold; (5) candidates that fail are cleared; recurring rejects signal threshold recalibration.

  **reflect-protocol vs. ingestion-protocol:** both write to the six memory surfaces via the same routing types, but are separate protocols. ingestion-protocol handles external resources — routing type must be *inferred* (classification work). reflect-protocol handles internal memory-candidates — routing type is *pre-declared* by the executor (validation work). Different triage; shared destination surfaces; no shared router needed. **The act of encoding produces emergent output.** Neither protocol is purely extractive — the process of debating what to encode, articulating connections, and fitting concepts into the existing architecture produces insights that weren't in the source material. Harvesting sessions demonstrate this consistently: the sleep test, compound reliability, and verifier's law all emerged from the encoding process itself, not from the resources being ingested. The encoding is generative, not just archival.

  **Queue time-to-live:** candidates that do not reach the recurrence threshold within N cycles (default: 3) are auto-rejected and cleared. Recurring rejects — the same candidate appearing and being rejected across multiple cycles — are a signal that either the formalization threshold is miscalibrated or the executor is mis-classifying. Both are improvement signals for the learning loop.

  reflect-protocol does no snapshot production — it is pure state consolidation.

- **Observe reasoning modes — abduction, deduction, induction:** Every protocol applies all three inference modes to its data source. The protocol is the *what* (which data to read); the inference mode is the *how* (how to reason about it).

  - **Abduction** — inference to the best explanation. "What would have to be true for this to make sense?" The detective mode; the creative move that generates hypotheses. Drives gap detection (isolated skill cluster → what's missing?), vestigial detection (skill never invoked → what explains it?), assumption interrogation (spec assumes X → what must hold for that to be true?).
  - **Deduction** — from declarations to necessary implications. Reading `depends_on` fields, backwards inference, schema validation. Zero-surprise: follows from structure alone. "A depends_on B and B is isolated → A is also blocked."
  - **Induction** — patterns from accumulated observations. Sequential pattern mining, calibration adjustment, formalization threshold (recurrence across 2+ independent artifacts). Confirms or rejects what abduction hypothesized.

  The cycle within Observe: anomaly surfaces → abduction generates hypothesis → induction checks it against pattern data → deduction extracts what follows necessarily → snapshot field written.

  **Context-gathering optimization principles** — already implicit in the design, named here for legibility:
  - *Information gain* — ask the question that collapses the most open assumptions at once. The "one precise question" to the user is information-gain maximization: surface the single unknown that would reduce the most uncertainty.
  - *Triangulation* — multiple independent sources confirming the same thing elevates confidence. The formalization threshold's "appeared in 2+ artifacts independently" is this principle applied to CLAUDE.md promotion.
  - *Minimum description length* — the best snapshot is the most compressed one that lets Orient proceed without ambiguity. Progressive disclosure is MDL applied to context injection.
  - *Saturation* — keep gathering until new sources stop producing new information. Context saturation bias: the user signals done, not Observe.

- **Coherence principles for module inclusion/pruning** (OODA-level principles apply; two Observe-specific additions):
  1. *Snapshot contribution* — every module's output must map to a named field in the snapshot. The snapshot is the only Observe output; work that doesn't reach it doesn't justify its existence. (Observe-specific instantiation of the output contribution principle.)
  2. *Context saturation bias* — the user is Observe's most expensive context source. Exhaust passive sources first (economics, not politeness). When turning to the user, prompt one question at a time but default to continuing — the user signals satiation, not Observe. Even when context seems sufficient, further prompting reliably surfaces ideas and constraints no passive source could provide.

**OODA cycle boundary — idle state and human-optional continuation:** When Act hands off to Observe and the dream state gap is zero (all acceptance criteria across all sub-projects satisfied), Observe enters the idle state. What happens next depends on context:

- **Interactive** — Observe surfaces the state to the user and waits. The user updates the dream state with new goals; a new cycle begins.
- **Partially autonomous** — Observe notifies (Slack, voice) and starts a timer. If the human intervenes before the timer expires, their input shapes the next cycle. If not, Observe autonomously selects the next sub-project and proceeds.
- **Fully autonomous** — Observe selects the next highest-leverage sub-project from the dream state backlog and starts a new cycle without human input. The dream state update is autonomous.
- **Headless / scheduled** — Observe notifies and idles until the next scheduled invocation or an explicit user signal.

Human involvement at the cycle boundary is context-dependent, not structurally required. The cycle boundary is the *opportunity* for human interaction — not a mandatory gate. The dream-protocol (voice session) is one Observe protocol for updating the dream state; autonomous selection from the backlog is another. The system never terminates; it cycles or idles.

---

**Proactivity system:** The harness can initiate work without a human prompt. Three trigger types:

| Trigger | Mechanism | Example |
|---------|-----------|---------|
| **Scheduled** | CronCreate/CronDelete — persistent, survives session boundaries | Daily learning-loop at 06:00; weekly pattern-roundup |
| **Event-driven** | Hooks — filesystem, lifecycle events | New inbox item → inbox-processor; loop completes → coherence check |
| **Threshold-based** | Metrics — value crosses a bound | quality_score drops below 0.7 → skill review; stale node count exceeds limit → topology scan |

**Modification semantics constraint on proactive execution:** the permission tier of the work being triggered determines the authorization model:

- **Freely modifiable** → fully autonomous; harness executes without notification
- **Meritocratic** → harness executes and notifies; human can intervene but work proceeds
- **Bilateral contract** → harness must ask before executing; no autonomous action

**Skill autonomy constraint:** `exploratory` skills are contraindicated for proactive execution regardless of tier. Exploratory work requires human presence to scope, redirect, or terminate — running it headless produces unbounded drift with no recovery signal. Proactive triggers must route to `scripted`, `guided`, or `heuristic` skills only. Note: Claude Code has an unshipped `AFK Mode` feature (autonomous mode when user is away, classified via transcript analysis) that may provide platform-native detection of pilot absence to automatically switch between interactive and autonomous operation.

**Heartbeat — autonomous background awareness.** Between human sessions, each org's harness runs a scheduled triage cycle that accumulates awareness so it arrives oriented when the human shows up. Two-tier cost model: depth-0 checks are rule-based and deterministic (inbox item count, artifact staleness, execution state changes, dream state gap closures, drop zone files) — zero LLM cost. When depth-0 detects signal, a single lightweight LLM call evaluates whether a full OODA cycle is warranted given the current dream state summary. No signal → suppress, zero cost. Signal → full autonomous OODA cycle. The triage checklist is a living artifact — updated by reflect-protocol and dream-protocol as the system's priorities shift, not a static file. What counts as signal evolves as the system learns. This is Observe at minimum depth, not a separate mechanism — the heartbeat, the session initialization protocol, and full Observe are the same phase at different resolutions.

**Proactive-messaging routing:** Proactivity does not introduce a new communication channel — it delegates to the existing proactive-messaging module. When a trigger fires, the harness evaluates the modification semantics tier of the work and routes accordingly: freely modifiable work completes silently and archives; meritocratic work completes then routes a notification through proactive-messaging (Slack, voice, etc.); bilateral work does not execute — the harness routes an escalation through proactive-messaging and waits for response before proceeding.
