No loop = the work category is literally outside the system's world. Not harder to reach — nonexistent within the system's action space. Decide cannot select a loop that doesn't exist; sub-agents cannot operate outside one. There is no soft floor below this: the Loop Library is the complete world boundary at every layer of the system. What you cannot think, you cannot do — and within this architecture, you can only think what has a loop. **Frontier operations** — working at the edge of the bubble: the named mode for operating at the capability boundary, where the Loop Library exists but the territory is novel. The meta-loop pushes the bubble outward.
- **Vocabulary and connections are the substrate of cognition; harvesting authors and maintains the ontology graph.** The dream state, the system design reference, per-org CLAUDE.md, and per-project wikis are all knowledge graphs of vocabulary terms and the connections between them — the same primitive as the org-level knowledge graph, applied recursively to itself. **The two-part structure**: vocabulary (named terms the system can think with) and connections (edges between them). Everything else — principles, recognitions, frameworks, diagnostics, the entry types defined in *Architectural Entry Standards* — is a *shape* of vocabulary entry, sharing the same underlying primitive (a name + a definition + a placement in the graph). **Harvesting does two things, not one**: it *authors* the graph when entering a new domain (a new org, a new project, a new system design subdomain) — minting the initial vocabulary that lets the system think about that domain at all — and it *maintains* the graph in established domains — adding new terms, drawing edges between existing ones, and promoting stable edges to vocabulary entries in their own right (a recurring "X IS Y" recognition starts as an edge between two terms and graduates to a named term as it stabilizes). The same rules that govern the org-level knowledge graph (orphan nodes are retrieval failures, every node needs ≥1 connection, content-addressable identifiers, typed relations) govern every layer. **The ontology is layered across the ecosystem**: universal terms live here, system-design-domain terms live in `REFERENCE-system-design.md`, per-org domain terms live in per-org CLAUDE.md and per-org knowledge graphs, per-project terms live in project wikis — the same harvesting protocol operates at all four layers and routes new terms to the right one. **The connections to existing principles are exact**: this is the operational mechanism for **Ashby's Law of Requisite Variety** (vocabulary IS the internal variety that matches environmental complexity), the substrate the **Conant-Ashby Good Regulator** is built from (the regulator's model is constructed from vocabulary; richer vocabulary → richer model → better regulation), the language-expansion side of the **Wittgensteinian boundary** (harvesting expands the world by adding words), and **everything-is-a-node graph unification** applied recursively to the dream state itself. **Naming is the move that turns invisible structure into reusable vocabulary, and reusable vocabulary is what compounds across cycles.** The "X IS structurally Y" recognitions in the system design reference are the canonical case: the harness was already a stream processor, saga framework, message broker, workflow orchestrator, and ML system, but until those names were minted, the equivalences weren't usable as thinking primitives. Operational detail — the entry-type taxonomy, the audit dimensions, the diagnostic question for routing candidates by shape — lives in *Architectural Entry Standards*.
- **Ashby's Law of Requisite Variety as theoretical foundation (cybernetics, 1956).** A system can only remain stable if its internal complexity matches the complexity of its environment. This is the unifying principle beneath multiple existing entries: the meta-loop expands the Loop Library when the Wittgensteinian boundary can't express the work (increasing variety); the primitive whiteboard shares primitives across orgs (pooling variety); agent horizon saturation demands the harness match the model's expanding capability (tracking variety); the digital garden cultivates concepts into primitives (growing variety organically); "lean by default, earn complexity" is the operational discipline (don't add variety you don't need yet). The law explains why the system must keep learning: when environmental complexity outpaces internal variety, the system decays. Curiosity is the fuel; the learning feedback loop is the mechanism; the knowledge graph is the variety store. A mind — or a harness — that contains multitudes will always outlast chaos. Reference: W. Ross Ashby, *An Introduction to Cybernetics*.
- **Conant-Ashby Good Regulator Theorem (cybernetics, 1970).** "Every good regulator of a system must be a model of that system." To control something, you must maintain an internal model of it. This dream state document is not optional documentation — it is the regulatory model that enables the system to self-govern. Without it, the system cannot steer toward its goals because it has no representation of what it's trying to be. The richer the model, the better the regulation: a one-page dream state produces crude self-governance; a deeply specified dream state with explicit intent, failure modes, and design principles produces precise self-governance. This is why harvesting sessions — spending hours enriching this document — directly improve the system's autonomous reliability. Every encoding is a refinement of the regulator. The same theorem explains why CLAUDE.md, the knowledge graph, and the six memory surfaces exist: each is a model of some aspect of the system (instructions, relationships, accumulated learning), and each enables regulation of that aspect. A system that stops modeling itself stops being able to govern itself. Reference: R. C. Conant and W. R. Ashby, "Every Good Regulator of a System Must Be a Model of That System."
- **Ultrastability (Ashby, 1952).** When simple feedback correction isn't enough, the system changes its own internal structure. This is qualitatively different from normal error correction: recovery tiers handle errors within the current structure (retry, scope reduction); ultrastability handles errors that reveal the structure itself is insufficient. The meta-loop is ultrastable — when no existing loop can express the work, it creates a new loop type, restructuring the system's vocabulary. Skill versioning is ultrastable — when a skill fails repeatedly, improvement proposals don't just retry, they upgrade the skill's internal procedure. The learning feedback loop is the ultrastability mechanism: it doesn't just correct outputs, it restructures the processes that produce outputs. Ordinary feedback says "the answer was wrong, try again." Ultrastability says "the process that produced the answer is wrong, restructure the process." The system that only corrects errors plateaus. The system that restructures itself in response to errors evolves. Reference: W. R. Ashby, *Design for a Brain*.
- **Ecological succession — success creates the conditions for its own obsolescence (Clements, 1916; Odum, 1969).** Ultrastability handles failure: restructure when the structure breaks. Succession handles the opposite: your success transforms the environment, making your current approach inappropriate *even though nothing failed*. Pioneer species colonize empty ground, modify the soil, and are replaced by species better suited to the soil they created. The pioneers don't fail — they succeed so thoroughly that they change the landscape into one where they no longer fit. In our architecture: the better a skill works, the faster it transforms the problem landscape into one where that skill is no longer the highest-leverage choice. Harvesting sessions hit stratum saturation not because they fail but because they succeed — practitioner content yields zeros because the architecture already absorbed those patterns. The remaining landscape is different terrain requiring different tools. This is why the digital garden needs continuous cultivation: not because things break, but because growth changes the soil. Skills, like pioneer species, should be designed with the expectation that their success makes them obsolete — and that this is a feature, not a failure. The meta-loop exists to populate the new landscape that succession creates.
- **Homeorhesis — maintaining trajectory, not equilibrium (Waddington, 1957).** Homeostasis maintains a fixed point; homeorhesis maintains a direction of travel. The dream state is not a static target the system converges to and holds — it's a trajectory through possibility space. These harvesting sessions prove it: the dream state keeps evolving, accumulating new encodings, shifting emphasis, growing richer. The system doesn't try to reach "done" and stop; it maintains a heading. This is why the dream state is a living document, not a specification. A specification converges; a trajectory sustains. The OODA cycle is the engine that maintains the trajectory — each cycle recalibrates direction based on new observations without ever arriving at a final destination.
- **Conversation Theory (Pask, 1970s).** Learning is synchronization of perspectives between two cognitive systems. The pilot-navigator relationship IS a Paskian conversation — two cognitive systems (human and agent) achieving mutual understanding through iterative interaction. Pask's **teachback** — teach another what you've learned to reveal gaps — is exactly what happens during encoding: the navigator articulates a concept, the pilot pushes back ("are you sure?"), gaps surface, understanding deepens for both. The encoding process itself is a conversation that produces emergent output (see ingestion-protocol). The three learning channels (doing, reading, dreaming) are three types of conversation: doing is conversation with the environment, reading is conversation with external minds, dreaming is conversation between pilot and navigator. Equifinality — multiple paths to the same understanding — is why these conversations work: pilot and navigator arrive at shared insight from different starting positions.
- **Structural Coupling (Maturana & Varela, 1980).** System and environment co-evolve through their history of interaction. Each shapes the other's possible futures. The architecture and the problems it tackles are structurally coupled — the architecture evolves because the problems change, and the problems we can address change because the architecture evolves. The pilot and navigator are structurally coupled — the pilot's thinking changes because of the navigator's capabilities, and the navigator's capabilities develop because of the pilot's direction. This is not one-way instruction; it's mutual transformation through ongoing interaction. Over time, structurally coupled systems develop a shared history that makes their interactions increasingly efficient — which is why the tenth harvesting session moves faster than the first.
- **Feedforward control — anticipation, not just reaction.** Feedback reacts to what happened. Feedforward anticipates what's coming. Orient doesn't just process what Observe captured — it models the trajectory and identifies where the system is heading. Decide doesn't just respond to Orient's assessment — it plans multiple moves ahead (the leverage protocol's multi-move planning). The dream state itself is the ultimate feedforward mechanism: it defines where the system should be going, so every cycle can steer toward it rather than just correcting from the last cycle's errors. Systems with only feedback oscillate. Systems with feedforward track smoothly. The combination of both — feedback (learning from what happened) and feedforward (steering toward the dream state) — is what gives the OODA cycle its characteristic stability under novel conditions. **Edge of chaos corollary:** the optimal operating point is the phase transition between too much structure (rigidity, can't adapt) and too little (chaos, can't sustain). This point moves as the system grows — what was the right amount of structure at 10 encodings is different at 27. The discipline is continuously recalibrating where the edge is, which is why "lean by default, earn complexity" is a practice, not a setting. **Metaregulation:** regulation of regulatory systems — the learning loop that improves skills is metaregulation. Ultrastability is metaregulation at the structural level; feedforward planning is metaregulation at the strategic level.
- **Games as cognitive waypoints** — a finite game is not just a bounded goal with a win condition and an artifact produced. It is a waypoint in a sequence of cognitive modes — you enter a mode of thinking, operate within it, and exit having moved through it. This reframes loop sequencing: Decide isn't just selecting which artifact to produce next, it's selecting which mode of thinking to enter next. The sequence of games is a sequence of cognitive stances the system passes through on the way to the dream state. You never play the same game twice — the game is the run, not the loop definition. The loop is the game type; each execution is a unique game because context, inputs, and state differ every time. The skill is the capability applied within the game to complete the task.

  The world expands through the full OODA cycle — dreaming is not a Library loop, it is the Observe phase:

  ```
  Observe (conceive) → eval loop (assess gap) → code loop (build)
         ↑___________________________________________________|
  ```

  - **Observe** — conceives the dream state. The voice session is the generative mechanism: human vision, intent, constraints, and direction enter the system here and nowhere else. The snapshot schema already captures everything needed: intent, priorities, open questions, gaps, assumptions, module states. No sub-agent in Act can generate human intent — dreaming belongs in Observe because dreaming is fundamentally human-facing. The dream state artifact produced by Observe is what eval loop assesses against and what Decide orients toward.
  - **eval loop** — maps the distance between the current world and the dream state. Gaps are only identifiable relative to the dream. Without a current dream state, eval loop can only find flaws in what exists — reactive optimization, not generative expansion.
  - **code loop** — closes specific gaps, including building new loop definitions that bring new vocabulary into the Loop Library as first-class executable entries. World boundary expansion happens here: code loop builds the loops that Decide will later select.

  **Loop Library = two classes: assessment and execution.** Dream state generation is not a Library class — it is an Observe responsibility, produced by voice sessions and maintained cycle-by-cycle. The Wittgenstein boundary is defined entirely by what eval loop and code loop can reach; Observe sets the target they navigate toward. The system is generative because Observe supplies vision; the Library is reactive because it executes against that vision. Both are necessary; neither should do the other's job. The meta-loop earns active status when loop *design* becomes complex enough to warrant specialized phases beyond what code loop provides — until then, building a new loop is engineering work with a specific target.

## Deferred Log

Items that are interesting but out of scope for current work. Revisit when the core system is stable.

| Item | Source | Rationale | Revisit when |
|------|--------|-----------|--------------|
| TLA+ formal verification of Act coordination | This session (2026-04-07) | TLA+ (Lamport) verifies concurrent/distributed systems exhaustively — exactly what Act's parallel coordination needs. Properties to verify: shadow clone path conflicts, dependency graph deadlock freedom, artifact collection completeness, two-layer WAL recovery correctness, phase transition ordering, atomic rename consistency. Concurrency bugs only manifest under specific timing conditions; TLA+ finds them exhaustively. Premature while the design is evolving — most valuable when the protocol stabilizes and before trusting it with unsupervised autonomous operation (dreamtime). | Act's coordination protocol is stable; dreamtime autonomous operation is being prepared; or a concurrency bug surfaces that testing can't reproduce |
| Lean formal verification as quality gate and trust strategy | This session (2026-04-07) | Lean is a formal theorem prover that can verify code correctness mathematically — not "does it pass tests" but "is it provably correct for ALL inputs." Three connections to the harness: (1) **Completion gaming resistance** — an agent can fake tests (write weak tests, remove failing ones) but cannot fake a formal proof. A Lean proof is the strongest possible quality gate, immune to the gaming failure modes the eval architecture must defend against. (2) **Trust elimination** — maps to the "Eliminate" trust strategy: you don't need to trust the agent's code if you can mathematically prove it satisfies the spec. Strongest form of deterministic prevention applied to code correctness. (3) **Verified code generation** — the trajectory (AlphaProof, LeanDojo, LLM-assisted proof generation) points toward agents producing code + proof as a paired artifact. The output isn't just code; it's code with a mathematical guarantee. Relevant for any domain where bugs are catastrophic: financial transactions (agent economy), smart contracts, auth/security code, infrastructure automation. The sovereign model registry could include a vertical model fine-tuned on Lean proof generation alongside code generation. | LLM-assisted Lean proof generation matures enough to be practical for real codebases; or a project domain requires formal correctness guarantees (financial, security, infrastructure); or the eval architecture needs a gaming-resistant verification tier |
| Networking protocol surface — MECE by OSI layer with per-ship mapping | This session | Full menu of relevant protocols across all 7 OSI layers, overlay networks, and cross-layer concerns (auth, encryption, disk). Per-ship protocol assignments for superorganism, servicegrid, pilgrimage, and dreamtime. Universal baseline vs. ship-specific vs. available-on-demand. Historical design lessons from protocol evolution. See companion document: `REFERENCE-networking-protocol-surface.md` | Harness networking capability is being designed; a new protocol integration is needed; inter-ship communication is being built |
| Agent economics / crypto vending machines | This session | Agents transact using crypto as machine-readable value transfer; vending machine model where agents buy specialized capabilities from each other. Future extension of Act's sub-agent model. **Payment primitives:** Two complementary rails now exist. *Traditional rails:* Stripe's Shared Payment Tokens (SPTs) — agent issues a token with usage limits and expiration, seller receives it, both sides get lifecycle events (granted → used → deactivated); JIT credential delegation applied to financial transactions. *Crypto rails:* x402 protocol (Coinbase, 50M+ transactions) — purpose-built machine-to-machine payment standard; agents pay for their own compute, API access, and storage autonomously; the concrete implementation of the vending machine model. *Hybrid rails:* Tempo Machine Payments Protocol (MPP, Stripe + Tempo L1, mainnet March 2026) — the session model is the key innovation: agent opens a session with a pre-authorized spending limit, thousands of micropayments aggregate into a single settlement, solving the per-transaction overhead that made micropayments impractical. Accepts fiat + crypto (stablecoins, cards, Lightning). SPTs are built into MPP. "OAuth for money" — maps naturally to loop executions (open session at loop start, consume paid services throughout, settle at completion). 100+ services integrated at launch. MPP is the most practical rail for high-frequency agent sessions; x402 for permissionless one-off payments; SPTs for credential delegation. Use all three, route by context. **Security posture:** private keys must live in TEEs (Trusted Execution Environments), never exposed to the agent's prompt or LLM context — this is the financial instantiation of the enclave isolation axis in our containment model. **Guardrails:** session caps and per-transaction limits are the financial equivalent of tool scoping — pre-authorized, bounded, auditable. Same pattern, different domain. **Tokenized agent ownership:** Virtuals Protocol is a concrete reference point — autonomous AI agents with tokenized ownership, where the agent itself is the asset. Extends the vending machine model from transactional (agents buying capabilities) to ownership (agents as investable entities with token-holders). **Broader tokenization thesis:** all assets will be tokenized — skills, artifacts, capabilities, data streams, agent time, compute access. The harness produces structured, high-quality, provenance-tracked artifacts; each is a candidate for tokenized exchange. The x402 payment rail is the transaction layer; tokenization is the asset layer above it. **Skills as agent onboarding:** in the agent economy, the way you onboard agent customers is by publishing skills, not documentation. A skill teaches an agent your API by giving it executable procedures rather than reference docs the human has to interpret and relay. Providers who publish skills get agent traffic; providers with only human-readable docs get hallucinated API calls. Every API provider will need to publish skills alongside their SDK — the skill IS the product manual, in a format the agent can execute. **Agent communication channels:** autonomous agents need their own communication infrastructure — email, wallets, identity. Candidates: AgentMail (agentmail.to — email inboxes for agents via API, MCP support, semantic search, Y Combinator backed) or programmatic email APIs (SendGrid, Resend) for email; payment rails already covered (x402, MPP, SPTs). The navigator having its own email address for receiving external reports, inter-org communication, and agent economy transactions is a natural requirement for always-on autonomous operation. **Arbitrage gap taxonomy — what agents scan for:** AI collapses arbitrage windows on the timescale of model releases; every closure opens new gaps. Five gap types that AI makes newly exploitable: (1) *Speed gaps* — one system updates slower than reality; the agent reacts faster than incumbents can reprice. (2) *Reasoning gaps* — public information available to everyone; the edge is interpreting it faster and acting before the crowd catches up. (3) *Fragmentation gaps* — the same thing priced differently in different places because nobody aggregates all sources; aggregation is near-free for LLMs. (4) *Discipline gaps* — identical strategy, 2x profit through perfect consistency (no fatigue, no emotional overrides, no missed actions). The harness IS a discipline gap closer — skills enforce consistency humans can't maintain. (5) *Knowledge asymmetry gaps* — intelligence arbitrage replaces labor arbitrage; the unit of value shifts from person-hour to outcome. **Upstream migration pattern:** when AI closes a gap, the new gap is always upstream — closer to judgment, taste, relationships, systems thinking; further from production, execution, information retrieval. The agent economy should target gaps where agents have structural advantage (discipline, speed, fragmentation, reasoning) and where upstream migration creates durable positions (systems architecture, not commodity production). Structural gaps (regulatory moats, relationship trust, physical logistics, genuine taste) resist AI compression; informational and cognitive gaps compress on a timescale of quarters. | Loop Library is stable and Act's sub-agent model is proven |
| Black box surfacing | Artifact Convention | Post-implementation documentation pass: make all mechanics, inputs, outputs, and module interactions explicitly visible. | System is built and stable |
| Environments taxonomy | This session | The harness operates in different types of environments, each requiring different support. Spectrum axis: how much of the harness's structural vocabulary does the environment already speak? Four known types: **Self-similar** — built with the harness from scratch; full OODA + primitives native; knowledge graph built in; primitive contribution to the whiteboard is mechanical. **Brownfield** — existing codebases not built with the harness; single or multi-repo; requires discovery protocol (see brownfield discovery protocol entry); primitives derived from code, schemas, API contracts. **Hybrid** — partially harness-native; some modules self-similar, some not; mixed approach. **External** — third-party systems you don't own or can't modify; interface-only access; primitives derived from public API contracts and documentation only. **Emergent** — the harness creates the environment rather than deploying into one; you lay out the structure and see what the agents create together; output is not predetermined but emerges from agent interaction within designed constraints; structurally different from the other four because the relationship is generative, not adaptive. The cellular automata / Game of Life analog: simple agents following local rules produce complex global behavior — the emergent environment is where this plays out. The designer sets the rules and constraints; the agents produce the patterns. What emerges is the artifact. **Any environment type can operate as an RL environment** — RL is a mode, not a type. Every environment produces training signal: self-similar from building, brownfield from adapting, emergent from what agents create together. Any can be intentionally configured for RL training with shaped reward functions. The richness of the training ecosystem across all environment types is the moat — not who has the biggest model, but who has the most interesting, richest ecosystem of tools, agents, and games to train within. Design environments that reward strategy diversity, not convergence — narrow environments produce agents with a narrow range of strategies; rich environments with multiple valid approaches and varied reward signals produce agents capable of genuinely different strategies. **Every environment has a meta** — the dominant strategy that currently produces the best results in that context. Orient's job includes identifying it. The response follows the investment model: follow the meta (More — it works, do more), improve it (Better — iterate on what works), or replace it (New — the meta is suboptimal, find a different one). Research taste is the capability for seeing past the meta to a genuinely different approach. **When constructing instances of any environment type**, three dimensions shape the agent's full environment: perspective (what the model inhabits — set by context engineering), habitat (the physical environment — isolation layers, tools, affordances), and cognitive runtime (the memory surfaces the agent operates within). These are already engineered separately throughout the architecture; together they inform how to design a complete environment for any type. Design principle: add environment support one at a time. Currently at zero formally supported; self-similar is the natural first (built by building the harness itself); brownfield is second. Environment type determines how primitives are extracted and contributed to the whiteboard — the environments taxonomy is the upstream design decision for the primitive whiteboard. | Core harness is stable and operating in multiple environment types; self-similar environment is the first to formalize |
| Sovereign data hub | This session | The data infrastructure layer that the primitive whiteboard, sovereign model registry, and brownfield discovery protocol all implicitly assume. A centralized integration point for sovereign data — bidirectional (ingest + serve), not just storage — that accumulates run archives, execution artifacts, calibration history, decision records, and improvement logs across all projects, environments, and harness instances. **Storage backend: PostgreSQL** — already in the infrastructure stack. Dolt-inspired patterns applied on top of PostgreSQL rather than adopting Dolt as a dependency: (a) *version control semantics* — temporal tables or event sourcing for full audit trail and time travel queries; (b) *cell-level conflict resolution* — concurrent agent writes resolved at field level using MVCC transactions, not file-level locking; (c) *content-addressable IDs* — hash-based identifiers (derived from UUIDs, not sequential) for collision-free distributed operation without central coordination; (d) *federation via database replication* — push/pull sync between org harness instances using PostgreSQL logical replication or pg_dump/restore, not file-level sync. Reference system: Beads (steveyegge/beads) — a distributed graph issue tracker built on Dolt that demonstrates these patterns at multi-agent scale; their migration from branch-per-worker to transaction-based shared-main (on advice from Dolt's co-founder) validates the MVCC-on-shared-main approach. **Initial implementation candidate: Neon** (serverless PostgreSQL with pgvector native). Three features align with harness needs: (a) *pgvector in PostgreSQL* — vector search + relational data in one store, no separate vector database; matches the "PostgreSQL + PG Vector" already specified in RAG strategies reference. (b) *Database branching (copy-on-write)* — the database equivalent of git worktrees for agents; each shadow clone gets its own database branch, experiments freely, merges results or discards failures; self-hosted PostgreSQL can't easily replicate this. (c) *Scale-to-zero* — our workload is bursty (intensive during loop execution, idle between); pay nothing when idle. Sovereignty tension: Neon is a hosted service. Sequencing heuristic applies — use Neon as starting infrastructure, learn from it, eventually replace with self-hosted sovereign PostgreSQL if needed. The branching capability is the most architecturally interesting feature and the hardest to replicate self-hosted. Two design goals not obvious from the consuming entries: (1) **multi-harness data pooling** — multiple harness instances (e.g. superorganism + servicegrid) contribute run data to a shared hub, making the training corpus richer than any single harness produces alone; (2) **sovereignty enforcement** — the hub is the operational enforcement point for data access control: which data is shared across orgs (flows to whiteboard) vs. which stays org-private (stays in hub). | Sovereign model registry and primitive whiteboard are being actively built; data infrastructure layer needs to be designed before those capabilities scale |
| Primitive whiteboard — shared cross-org primitive library | This session | A shared knowledge graph between a network of harnesses — the multi-harness extension of what each harness already maintains locally. Each org runs its own harness; the whiteboard is what they share: a shared pool of the four capability primitives (protocols, frameworks, skills, evals) across org harness instances. Example: superorganism and servicegrid each have their own harness — they contribute generic primitives to the shared whiteboard and pull from it. Org-specific primitives stay private; generic domain primitives (auth skills, architecture frameworks, code review protocols, quality evals) flow into the shared pool. The selection mechanism already handles curation — quality_score and usage signal determine which primitives rise. Network effect: more orgs → richer shared library → better selection for all. Reuse patterns the whiteboard enables: (1) *Context injection* — pull a relevant skill or framework from the whiteboard into a sub-agent's context; smaller and more targeted than injecting the full knowledge graph. (2) *Sovereign model training signal* — primitives in the whiteboard are structured, high-quality training examples for fine-tuning domain-specific sovereign models. (3) *RAG retrieval corpus* — sovereign models query the whiteboard at inference time. (4) *Brownfield pattern-matching* — during discovery of a new environment, match observed patterns against whiteboard primitives to recognize familiar domains without starting from scratch. (5) *Pseudolanguage vocabulary extension* — a framework or protocol on the whiteboard defines domain-specific vocabulary for a new dialect. No new artifact type required — the four primitives are the unit of exchange. | Multiple org harness instances are active and cross-org primitive sharing becomes demonstrably valuable |
| Sovereign graph system — Obsidian + graph query engine | This session (2026-03-29) | The knowledge graph needs two interfaces: human-browsable (visual garden for the pilot) and machine-queryable (graph algorithms for topology-protocol). Long-term vision: a single sovereign system that combines Obsidian's visual garden experience with Neo4j-class graph query capability — community detection, betweenness centrality, shortest path, cluster analysis — all local, all owned. **Starting point (immediate):** open the orchestrator repo as an Obsidian vault. The files are already there — dream state, skills, memory, CLAUDE.md. Formalize the link structure with explicit `[[wiki-links]]` so Obsidian's graph view and Claude Code's grep can both traverse the graph. The digital garden lifecycle (plant, cultivate, formalize) operates here. **Scope: org-level, not project-level.** Each org (superorganism, servicegrid, pilgrimage, dreamtime) is a parent directory of project repos. The Obsidian vault sits at the org level, giving the pilot a visual graph across all projects within that org — dream state, skills, memory, decision traces, knowledge graph, all browsable and linked. Obsidian is the org-level visual interface for the human pilot. Independent convergence: Jerry Liu (LlamaIndex CEO) arrived at the same pattern — Obsidian for locally generated markdown, artifacts as context carriers between sessions — despite building RAG infrastructure professionally. A vote for file system + knowledge graph over vector RAG as the primary retrieval layer. **Architectural constraint:** markdown files remain the source of truth at every stage. Any graph database is a derived index, never the primary store. If the database dies, rebuild from files. Sovereignty means the simplest layer is the durable one. **Migration path:** Obsidian vault (now) → add lightweight graph library in Python for topology-protocol queries (when file-based traversal gets expensive) → full sovereign graph system (when primitive whiteboard needs multi-harness shared graph access). **Implementation candidate: Graphiti** (github.com/getzep/graphiti, MIT license, self-hostable on Neo4j) — temporal knowledge graph for agent memory with bi-temporal fact tracking, contradiction handling via invalidation not deletion, incremental updates, and MCP server integration. Reference implementation to learn from; evaluate when the lightweight graph library step proves insufficient. The sovereign data hub entry covers the storage backend; this entry covers the graph-specific query and visualization layer that sits on top. **Setup notes:** (1) Tags as nodes, not labels — concept notes with their own connections enable graph traversal; flat tags don't. (2) Taxonomy file at vault root as source of truth, referenced from CLAUDE.md. (3) Wiki-links over prose references — explicit `[[links]]` are traversable by both Obsidian graph view and Claude Code grep. (4) Git-backed vault for version control and async updates. | Topology-protocol needs real graph algorithms (betweenness, community detection) that file-based traversal can't efficiently provide; or primitive whiteboard needs shared graph access across harness instances |
| Hypernetworks for instant model adaptation (Sakana AI) | Sakana AI research (2026) | Two complementary hypernetwork methods, both sub-second latency, single forward pass: **Doc-to-LoRA** compresses long documents into LoRA adapter weights — converting context-level knowledge into weight-level knowledge (zero per-inference cost). Near-perfect accuracy at 5x native context window. **Text-to-LoRA** generates task-specific LoRA adapters from natural language task descriptions — a skill definition becomes an adapter that makes the model inherently better at that skill without consuming context. This is the ERL internalization step made literal: skill → LoRA → the model does it natively. Architectural relevance: (1) navigator's domain expertise → adapter weights instead of context tokens; (2) skill definitions → task-specific adapters, freeing context window for actual work; (3) the meta-pattern (network generates weights for another network) mirrors the meta-architecture (system generates configuration for another system). The "cost amortization" principle: pay meta-training cost once, generate adapters on demand. Evaluate alongside RLM and LCM when sovereign models are in use. Code: github.com/SakanaAI/Doc-to-LoRA, github.com/SakanaAI/Text-to-LoRA | Sovereign model registry is active; serving costs at scale justify weight-level knowledge compression |
| Compute infrastructure trajectory (tech-tree path) | SpaceX/xAI announcement (2026-02) | Four-tier compute trajectory as tech-tree nodes: **Tier 1: External API** (current — Claude API, pay per token). **Tier 2: Sovereign local** (deferred — vLLM + fine-tuned models, data privacy, custom training). **Tier 3: Sovereign cloud** (future — own models, own cloud infrastructure, multi-region). **Tier 4: Space-based** (far future — orbital data centers, solar-powered, unlimited energy). Each tier transition unlocks different capabilities and changes the cost calculus. Key claim from SpaceX/xAI: "within 2-3 years, lowest cost AI compute will be in space." Energy is the ultimate constraint on terrestrial AI scaling — "global electricity demand for AI cannot be met with terrestrial solutions, even in the near term." The CIEL framework's Energy pillar predicts this bottleneck: as Intelligence substitutes Labor, compute (Energy) becomes the binding constraint. Space-based compute is the Kardashev-scale resolution. Near-term relevance: the tier 1→2 transition (external → sovereign) is the actionable next step; tiers 3-4 inform long-horizon strategic planning. **Micro-macro metric pair:** ship velocity (how quickly one ship makes progress through possibility space) is the micro metric; Kardashev level (civilization's total compute capacity to explore possibility space) is the macro equivalent. The system optimizes for ship velocity; the civilization optimizes for Kardashev advancement. Same axis, different scale. | Tier 2 (sovereign local) is the immediate next node; revisit tier 3-4 when sovereign infrastructure is operational. See `REFERENCE-scaling-laws.md` for the full taxonomy of known and candidate scaling laws across all eras and substrates |
| Open hardware stack — substrate sovereignty trajectory | This session (2026-04-08) | The open hardware stack matured quietly over the last 5 years and makes literal substrate sovereignty (own kernel + own chip) achievable on a much shorter horizon than "effectively infinite." Distinct from the Compute infrastructure trajectory entry above — that's about *where the model runs* (deployment); this is about *who designs the silicon and OS the harness runs on* (substrate). Both are sovereignty concerns; they're different knobs. **Open hardware stack inventory:** (1) **RISC-V** — fully open ISA; download a working CPU design, modify it, call it yours. No licensing, no NDA. (2) **Yosys + nextpnr** — open-source FPGA synthesis toolchain; HDL → bitstream without proprietary vendor tools. Free. (3) **OpenLane** — open-source RTL-to-GDSII flow; production-quality ASIC design pipeline. (4) **Skywater 130nm PDK** — open-source process design kit released by Google in 2020; the first open foundry PDK at a usable node. (5) **Tiny Tapeout** (Matt Venn) — multi-project shuttle service; submit a small chip design, get real silicon mailed back for a few hundred dollars. Real packaging, real testing. (6) **Efabless** — larger open shuttles, ~$10K per design for more substantial chips. **Open OS stack:** SerenityOS (Andreas Kling, started 2018) and other hobby kernels demonstrate that solo OS development is achievable with months of dedicated work; AI copilots collapse the bar further. **Honest horizon table:**

  | Tier | When | What it looks like |
  |---|---|---|
  | Today | 2026 | Solo RISC-V soft-core on FPGA in a weekend (~$200); ASIC on Skywater for ~$300 in months via Tiny Tapeout |
  | 5 years | 2031 | Solo full-stack: own shell + own kernel + own RISC-V chip routine for serious operators |
  | 10 years | 2036 | AI-designed verified ASICs at smaller nodes; substrate becomes a swap-week-not-swap-decade |
  | 20 years | 2046 | Substrate sovereignty routine for any motivated individual |

  **Three accelerants compounding:** (1) AI-assisted RTL generation — GPT-4-class models already write basic Verilog; AlphaProof-class formal reasoning is maturing; the combination produces verified RTL on a tractable near-term horizon. (2) Smaller open PDKs — Skywater 130nm is the current floor; credible paths to open 65nm and 45nm in the next 5–10 years. (3) AI-assisted OS development — SerenityOS-style work with AI copilots is already close to working; the harness's own compounding capability eventually contributes to its own substrate via "the system is its own first customer." **Strange-loop angle:** as the harness matures, it can build more of its own substrate. Substrate sovereignty becomes a *consequence* of harness maturity rather than a separate program. The stopping problem inverts — you don't decide how far down to descend; you descend as far as the current generation of the harness makes cheap. Each generation pushes the floor lower. **Connection to 11-knob sovereignty framing** (Architecture, line ~388): the Substrate knob is the slowest knob, not an unreachable one. Open-source-substrate (bash, Linux, ext4) is the *current waypoint*, sovereign-enough because the implementations are open and not under adversarial control. Literal substrate sovereignty is the longer-horizon trajectory. | Literal substrate sovereignty becomes a concrete project rather than a horizon; or AI-assisted hardware design tooling matures enough to make solo chip design routine; or an org needs hardware sovereignty for compliance/security reasons |
| Sovereign model registry | This session | A registry of models trained on sovereign data — owned, versioned, and controlled by the operator, not dependent on external providers. **Three capability tiers:** (1) fine-tuning external base models on sovereign data (near-term), (2) training models from scratch using RL or whatever techniques are best at the time (mid-term, sovereign all the way down), (3) deliberative alignment — feeding specifications (skill definitions, CLAUDE.md, model spec) as both training material and eval material to grade and reinforce model behavior against the system's intentions (applicable at both tiers). Two key architectural implications: (1) **Data flywheel** — every loop execution produces labeled training data: spec → artifact, rubric → quality score, failure patterns → failure labels. **Training mechanism: environment-driven RL** — instead of rebuilding the harness as a sandboxed training environment, a recording proxy on the inference path captures production traces and derives reward signal directly from execution. The orchestrator interacts with the system as a user would; no separate sandbox needed. This is how Cursor ships improved model checkpoints every 5 hours. The harness's existing execution traces (tool calls, artifacts, quality scores, decision traces) ARE the training data — the recording proxy formalizes collection without a separate data pipeline. **Trace triage via lightweight signals** (Signals, arxiv 2604.00356): not all traces are equally valuable for training. Seven cheap signals computed from execution metadata (no LLM calls) identify informative trajectories: misalignment, stagnation, disengagement, satisfaction, failure, loop, exhaustion. Signal-based sampling achieves 82% informativeness vs. 54% random — 1.5x more efficient per informative trace. These signals are computable from metadata the harness already produces (tool calls, phase transitions, token usage, completion status). Also useful for Act's runtime monitoring: detecting stagnation, loops, and exhaustion in real-time signals a shadow clone is in trouble before it burns its token budget. This corpus is small but domain-rich — the bridge to training vertical models is **synthetic continued pre-training**: generate large synthetic datasets (Q&A pairs, rephrased versions, entity-relationship descriptions) from the small sovereign corpus, then train on the synthetic data. Research shows this outperforms direct fine-tuning and can match GPT-4 on domain tasks with ~1B synthetic tokens generated from a small source corpus. RL-based training is more parameter-efficient than SFT for this (even tiny parameter counts improve RL performance), favoring RL approaches for sovereign model training. This corpus trains sovereign models. The primitive whiteboard provides additional high-quality structured training examples. More execution → richer corpus → better fine-tuned models → better execution. The primitive library and model registry co-evolve: primitive versioning improves procedures; model fine-tuning improves underlying capability. Two compounding flywheels simultaneously. (2) **Model selection as an extended dimension of skill selection** — Act currently co-selects skill + model tier (Haiku/Sonnet/Opus); a sovereign registry adds a third axis: which fine-tuned model from the registry best fits this task + data type. Sits as a layer in the stack: vLLM (serving infrastructure, already deferred) → sovereign model registry (model management) → RL for primitive selection (selection mechanism evolution, already deferred). Deployment constraint: sovereign models are required when data cannot be exposed to external APIs (legal, compliance, competitive) — the architecture must support routing sensitive tasks to sovereign models while routing others to external APIs. (3) **Vertical models via domain-specific post-training on open-source base models** — take open-source foundations (Gemma, Llama, Qwen, Mistral) and post-train on domain-specific sovereign data to produce vertical models tuned to specific org capabilities (servicegrid logistics, pilgrimage game design, etc.). Each org could have its own vertical model optimized for its domain. (4) **Agent lab** — an autonomous business unit (potentially its own org alongside superorganism, servicegrid, pilgrimage, dreamtime) that trains sovereign models as its primary output. The lab runs its own OODA cycles: observes training data and model performance, orients on what vertical models are needed, decides training strategies, acts by executing training runs and evals. It produces vertical models the way servicegrid produces logistics capabilities — training is its product, models are its artifacts. Connects to the agent economy (models as tradeable artifacts), the environments taxonomy (the lab IS an emergent RL environment), and dreamtime (autonomous exploration of model training space without human in Observe). | Ready to move off external-only API model; data flywheel has accumulated sufficient run data to produce meaningful fine-tuning signal. RL framework selection: see companion document `REFERENCE-rl-training-frameworks.md` |
| Sovereign agent language | This session (2026-04-07) | The sovereign-all-the-way-down trajectory extends to the language agents execute in. TypeScript is the current integration; a sovereign language is the destination. Tech-tree path: TypeScript SDK (expose harness capabilities as typed modules) → DSL layer embedded in TypeScript (harness concepts as first-class syntax — skills, loops, phases, gates, permission semantics, structured I/O) → sovereign language (full language designed for agent operations, trained into sovereign models). Each step reveals the friction points that inform the next. The sovereign model registry is the prerequisite — a custom language only works when you control the model that writes it. The language and the model co-evolve: the language is designed for agent operations, the model is trained to be native in it. No external dependency on TypeScript/V8/Node ecosystem at the end state. | Sovereign model registry is active and the TypeScript SDK is built, revealing whether a DSL layer would reduce friction |
| Local model serving: vLLM over Ollama | Red Hat benchmark | When moving to locally hosted models, use vLLM not Ollama. Benchmark: vLLM 793 TPS vs. Ollama 41 TPS (20× difference), 80ms vs. 673ms P99 latency. Ollama caps at 4 parallel requests by default and doesn't scale; vLLM uses dynamic batching and scales linearly with concurrency. Ollama is fine for single-user local dev; vLLM is the correct choice for any multi-agent concurrent workload. | Ready to move off Claude API to locally hosted models |
| LLM resource scheduling for parallel agents | AgentOS | When Act spawns concurrent sub-agents, they compete for API capacity: rate limit contention, cost overrun risk, uneven token budget distribution across tasks in flight. Token budget allocation per task, priority queuing, and rate limit coordination are kernel-level scheduling concerns not currently addressed. AgentOS names this explicitly as a required kernel function — the gap becomes visible at concurrent agent scale. Note: Claude Code has an unshipped `TOKEN_BUDGET` feature (per-session or per-agent token spend cap) that may address this at the platform level. | Act's parallel coordination is built and concurrent agent scale becomes a bottleneck |
| Bounty board (best-of-N task execution) | Claude background agents | Task board and bounty board are the same architecture with different N. Each task has `n: int = 1`; N=1 is current behavior. N>1 spawns N agents running the same skill in parallel, judges all artifacts against the skill rubric, takes the highest-scoring result. Strictly dominates task board for high-ambiguity, ephemeral/maintained artifacts with no external side effects. Task board dominates for permanent-reversibility tasks (N deploys = disaster). Best-of-3 captures most quality gain; marginal returns diminish sharply beyond N=3. Limiting factor is cost (N× tokens). Becomes obviously worth doing when token costs drop another order of magnitude. | Token costs make N>1 economical at scale; Act's parallel coordination is proven |
| Unified primitive format alignment | DREAM-STATE manifests + existing SKILL.md format + unified invocation | The four manifest schemas (skill, framework, protocol, eval) defined in DREAM-STATE-ooda.md need to be reconciled into one canonical SKILL.md format with a `type` field distinguishing them. The unified invocation principle (all four stored as SKILL.md, invoked via Skill tool) is now encoded in the Loop Library section. Implementation work: (1) define the canonical frontmatter that covers all four types (shared fields + type-specific fields), (2) reconcile with the actual SKILL.md format in skills-library-mcp, (3) migrate existing skills, (4) create the directory convention (protocols/, frameworks/, loops/{loop}/skills/, evals/). | Unified format is designed and ready to implement; skills-library-mcp is being updated |
| Linux as canonical execution environment | This session (2026-04-06) | The trajectory points toward Linux as the canonical environment for all autonomous execution. Cloud sandboxes (E2B, Daytona), containers, CI/CD, sovereign model serving (vLLM), and dreamtime (fully autonomous) are all Linux. macOS remains load-bearing for the pilot's Observe surface (daily driver, Computer use via Desktop, iOS development). The natural split: macOS for the pilot, Linux for everything the harness executes autonomously. Currently, local shadow clones run on the pilot's macOS machine — so this split isn't actionable until cloud sandbox spawning is in use or the pilot moves to Linux. The bash shell convention (encoded in Act's shadow clone section) is the first concrete step: it makes the macOS pilot environment generate commands compatible with Linux clone environments. Full migration means the pilot's machine is Linux too — a personal preference decision, not an architectural one. The architectural decision is: Linux is the target execution environment for shadow clones. | Cloud sandbox spawning (E2B, Daytona) is in active use; or persistent clones run on remote infrastructure; or the pilot considers moving to Linux |
| PreCompact hook limitations | This session (2026-04-06) | The dream state's `PreCompact` hook strategy — "inject a directive before compaction fires that identifies high-value cache anchors and instructs the post-compaction agent to re-read them" — may be overstated. Claude Code's `PreCompact` hook is observational only: it can observe that compaction is about to happen but cannot inject instructions into the summarization process or block it. Compaction is a platform-controlled concern. The harness can observe but not direct it. A sovereign agent runtime where compaction is an extension surface (Pi's `custom-compaction` extension pattern: replace the default compaction with a cheaper model or custom strategy) would resolve this. Additionally: compaction preserves the system prompt cache (same bytes, same hash) and only invalidates the conversation portion — the cost of cache-breaking from compaction is narrower than "breaks the prompt cache" suggests. | Pi agent evaluation; or sovereign agent runtime is being designed; or compaction strategy for sustained autonomous operation is being built |
| Ecosystem CLAUDE.md bilateral rewrite | This session | The global CLAUDE.md (`~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`) was written before the OODA architecture matured and is now stale. Three sections need updating: (1) Terrain Check — "uphill/downhill" checklist → policy entropy framing: high entropy → surface one precise gap (information-gain maximization); low entropy → proceed. (2) Deep Context Protocol — misattributed to Orient; in the mature architecture this is Observe behavior. Orient applies frameworks, does not gather raw data. "10+ turns" and question category checklists fight the "one precise question / conversational feel" principle. (3) Learning Feedback Loop (Act) — "learning-loop" no longer exists; Act executes; reflect-protocol handles memory consolidation; Observe handles measurement. Must be done together, section by section, bilateral consent before writing. Also: assumption-of-breach axiom currently lists three containment axes — update to four (network egress control added this session). **Design constraints from research (ETH Zurich evaluating-agent-mds, SkillBench, Claude Code source leak analysis, 2026-04):** (a) *Compliance decay curve* — 95% compliance at 1-2 messages, 60-80% at 3-5, 20-60% at 6-10, downhill after 10. Implications: session length affects instruction adherence; long sessions need /compact or /clear at natural boundaries; the most critical instructions must be the most concise to survive decay. (b) *"May or may not be relevant" injection* — Claude Code's system prompt explicitly tells the model: "this context may or may not be relevant to your task. You should not respond to this context unless it is highly relevant to your task." Every line in CLAUDE.md must earn its place — generic or verbose content is actively deprioritized by the harness itself. The more bloated the file, the more likely critical instructions get ignored alongside irrelevant ones. (c) *Instruction budget (~100-150 after system prompt)* — LLMs follow roughly 150-200 distinct instructions with reasonable consistency; Claude Code's system prompt consumes ~50 of those. The remaining ~100-150 is the total budget across all CLAUDE.md levels (ecosystem + org + project). Every instruction competes with every other instruction for this budget. Current user-level CLAUDE.md likely exceeds this alone. Refactor strategy: user-level should be 10-15 lines max (Boris keeps his at 2); verbose content moves to skills (progressive disclosure — loaded on demand, not always-on) or project-level files. (d) *Auto-generated context hurts* — ETH Zurich found auto-generated agent.md files decreased success rate by 3% and increased cost by 20%. Only carefully curated, failure-driven content helps. SkillBench found curated skills improved pass rates by 16.2 percentage points while self-generated skills added zero benefit. Validates our "harvest our own" convention. | Next dedicated session |
| Interactive notebook workbench | This session (2026-03-29) | Jupyter notebook as the ephemeral exploration complement to the Obsidian vault (persistent garden). The vault is where things grow; the notebook is where you experiment. Connect via MCP to Claude Code and the vault — notebook can query the knowledge graph, invoke skills, analyze execution metrics, visualize graph structure. Voice integration (Jupyter Whisper pattern) for rapid pilot interaction. The notebook is the Observe/Orient workbench; the vault is long-term memory; Claude Code is the execution engine; MCP is the protocol layer. Don't build our own — use Jupyter's ecosystem. When exploration produces an insight worth keeping, plant it in the vault. | Obsidian vault is operational and the pilot wants interactive data analysis / experimentation beyond what Claude Code chat provides |
| Invented memory — open memory architecture | Hyper-agents paper (Meta AI, 2025), this session (2026-03-29) | A self-improving agent starting with nothing (bash + file edit + LLM) independently discovered that it needed persistent memory — and invented its own memory tool storing scores, insights, and meta-hypotheses about how to improve. Nobody told it memory was needed. This validates our designed memory architecture (seven surfaces, knowledge graph, run archives) from the opposite direction: top-down design and bottom-up discovery converge on the same conclusion. The provocative implication: **designed core + open invention slot.** Keep the six memory surfaces as stable foundation, but add an open channel where the system can create new memory structures when it discovers needs we didn't anticipate. The meta-loop already creates new loops; this is the memory equivalent. Specific gap the paper reveals: the agent stored meta-hypotheses about how to COMPOSE insights across iterations ("combine Gen 55's critical reasoning with Gen 65's balance"). Our system stores individual improvement proposals but doesn't systematically store hypotheses about how to combine learnings across runs. That's the invented memory structure we're missing. | Meta-loop is operational and the system can experiment with inventing memory structures; or self-improvement architecture is being actively designed |
| RAG retrieval strategies | Cole Medin (this session, 2026-03-29) | 11 RAG strategies mapped to architectural systems with recommended combinations per use case. See companion document: `REFERENCE-rag-strategies.md` | Sovereign data hub retrieval layer is being built; or topology-protocol needs retrieval beyond file-based grep |
| Autonomous business taxonomy | Hormozi business shapes (this session, 2026-03-29) | Four business shapes as a taxonomy for autonomous operation readiness — which types of businesses can the harness eventually run without a human? **Software** (most ready): the harness already builds software; closing the loop means autonomous product management, user feedback processing, deployment, and iteration. **E-commerce** (high readiness): supply chain, inventory forecasting, ad optimization, and customer service are largely data-driven and automatable. Constraint (cash flow/supply chain) is quantitative. **Education** (medium readiness): content creation, course delivery, community management are automatable; the retention/stickiness constraint requires understanding human psychology but can be addressed with feedback loops. **Service** (least ready): talent is the bottleneck, and teaching humans is fundamentally harder to automate. But the TEACHING component (onboarding, training, SOP creation) is where the harness excels. Each shape has a characteristic growth curve, a core constraint, and a different autonomy profile. Dreamtime's first ventures should target the shapes with highest autonomy readiness. The Hormozi framework also maps to what the harness would need at each stage: the sleep test validates basic autonomy, the 13-week cash flow system maps to Observe's financial monitoring, and the "features not bugs" mindset prevents the system from fighting its own business shape. | Dreamtime org is operational and selecting its first autonomous business ventures |
| Detection latency as attack surface | Snyk OODA blog | At current session-speed operation, cycle time isn't a security bottleneck. At scale — continuous operation, concurrent sub-agents, live network access — the window between an adversarial event and Observe's next cycle is an attack dwell window. Cycle time becomes a security metric: slow Observe = longer undetected malicious activity. Design question: when the harness moves to continuous/autonomous operation, what detection loop speed is required, and does the current Observe cycle boundary satisfy it? | Harness moves to continuous or autonomous operation |
| Review skill class for the audit-loop | Claude Code Review | Review skills are a specialization within the audit-loop: each skill scopes to one concern class (security, correctness, regressions, conventions), the fleet deploys in parallel, findings are deduplicated and ranked by severity. This is more powerful than a single generalist verifier — specialization-by-concern lets each agent go deep on its class without diluting attention across all classes. REVIEW.md steers which skills fire and what they check, functioning as the loop-specific config (analogous to the steerable reading principle in Observe). Bidirectional CLAUDE.md consistency is a built-in concern for this skill class: code changes that make CLAUDE.md outdated should be flagged alongside code issues — spec and code drift in both directions. Implement when the audit-loop is being built out. | Audit-loop is active and PR-triggered workflows are in use |
| Sub-agent self-compaction at iteration boundaries | Ralph guide / loop layers companion | Deep skills may legitimately exceed a single context window across multiple iterations. The architectural response is not to cap skill depth but to enable sub-agents to self-compact at natural checkpoints — specifically after completing a layers:N iteration. The compaction at iteration boundary mirrors the cycle-level compaction design: preserve decisions made, constraints discovered, and what was produced; discard intermediate reasoning. Without self-compaction, a long-running sub-agent accumulates context debt across iterations until it degrades or fails. Implement alongside loop layers — the iteration boundary is the compaction trigger. Same design principles as PreCompact hook apply at the sub-agent level. | Loop layers is implemented; loops:N with deep skills hits context ceiling in practice |
| "Show me" — computer use demonstration as Visual loop skill class | This session | A named UX pattern for the Visual loop: instead of the agent describing something in text, it demonstrates by doing it on screen — computer use + screen recording as the output artifact. Distinct from Remotion (programmatic post-run summaries assembled from data); this is live demonstration, agent actually performing the task on screen. Three named use cases: *code review* — agent navigates to each issue in context rather than listing it; *how-to demonstration* — agent performs the workflow while narrating; *inspiration* — agent explores and shows something interesting as visual discovery. Skill class: input spec is "show me how to do X" or "review this PR visually"; output is a screen recording; self-eval checks whether the demonstration clearly showed the target behavior. Extension: voice narration + computer use produces a fully agent-authored tutorial artifact. | Visual loop is active and computer use is available as a tool |
| Remotion video summaries | Personal use | Programmatic video summaries of completed sub-projects and significant loop runs — produced by a Remotion skill within the Visual loop. Use cases: sub-project completion recap, capability milestone summaries, personal archive. Not a default completion artifact; triggered on-demand or when a sub-project is flagged for summary. Implement as a Visual loop skill once the Visual loop is active. | Visual loop is built out and core system is stable |
| Encoding yield per resource type | Resource ingestion protocol | Track average encodings per resource type to inform prioritization — which types to invest harvest depth in, which to scan quickly. Current hypothesis: ~50% of resources yield 0–1 encodings, ~50% yield 2–3, <1% yield 4+. One-liners are a disproportionately high-yield type (2–4 encodings relatively easily) despite being the shortest. The 50/50 split means the harvest strategy is: scan quickly to detect which bucket a resource falls into, then go deep once early signal appears — fast rejection still matters for the low-yield half, but depth investment is justified for a large share of resources. Requires accumulated ingestion data to validate the hypothesis and compute yield by type. | Enough ingestion cycles have run to compute yield rates per resource type |
| Resource lifecycle states — exhausted vs. re-usable | Resource ingestion protocol | Resources have at least two lifecycle states: *exhausted* (fully harvested against the current system; re-ingesting now yields nothing new) and *re-usable* (high potential for a different harvest as the system matures — potent one-liners especially; "no AI steps in the same river twice"). The design challenge is working out the full permaculture of resource recycling: in permaculture, nothing is waste — the same material yields different value depending on what's needed, what else is available, and the season. Applied here: the same resource may be exhausted against the harness architecture but abundant for a new project; exhausted for framework extraction but re-usable for skill harvest; correctly classified as a one-liner today but worth re-reading as a structured document once the domain has matured enough to recognize its depth. Multiple recycling mechanisms exist depending on routing target, system maturity, and current gaps — designing the full set requires accumulated signal about which patterns actually emerge in practice. | Ingestion protocol is stable; multiple ingestion cycles have accumulated enough signal to see what recycling patterns emerge |
| Project/repo-level ingestion routing | Resource ingestion protocol | The ingestion-protocol currently assumes a single target (harness architecture). A routing layer that classifies each resource or harvest item by target level — harness architecture, specific project, specific repo — and routes accordingly would make the protocol general-purpose. The resource taxonomy (already encoded in Entry Cases) handles the harvest-mechanism layer; this deferred item is the destination-routing layer above it. Resources re-ingestible: the same input produces a different harvest as the architecture and skill libraries evolve ("no AI steps in the same river twice"), so re-running potent resources against a more mature system is a native use case the routing layer should support. | Core ingestion-protocol is stable and multi-project operation is active |
| Multi-level agents (persistent tiers) | This session | A second tier of persistent agent scoped to a project/app. Currently, navigators are the only persistent agent (org-scoped). A project-scoped persistent agent would maintain its own context across sessions within a single project, without the navigator's org-wide scope. Could be relevant for Dreamtime or any project large enough that the navigator's scope is too broad for project-level continuity. | A project outgrows what a single navigator can hold in context; likely Dreamtime first |
| Agent society | This session | Persistent multi-agent teams within a bounded context (e.g., an app) with ongoing relationships and mutual awareness. Qualitatively different from shadow clones: society members are persistent, have different specializations, and maintain awareness of each other's work. **Claude Code implementation foundation: agent teams** (experimental, `CLAUDE_CODE_EXPERIMENTAL_AGENT_TEAMS`). Agent teams provide: shared task list with self-coordination and dependency tracking, peer-to-peer messaging (teammates message each other directly, not just report to lead), lead agent that coordinates work and synthesizes results, `TeammateIdle`/`TaskCreated`/`TaskCompleted` hooks for quality gates, plan approval workflow (lead reviews teammate plans before execution), in-process or split-pane (tmux/iTerm2) display modes. Key constraints: no nested teams (teammates can't spawn teams), lead is fixed for team lifetime, one team per session. Transition point from subagents: when parallel workers need to communicate with each other rather than just report back. | Coordination protocol is tested with persistent multi-agent teams; a project needs multiple persistent specialized agents; Claude Code agent teams feature graduates from experimental. Also note: Claude Code has an unshipped `Peer Discovery` feature (find other Claude instances on your machine via Unix domain sockets) that may enable direct inter-agent discovery without a central orchestrator. |
| Pseudolanguage dialect structure | This session | The Loop Library as pseudolanguage already encoded at "Loop Library as pseudolanguage vocabulary." This extends it: a family implies a root language with form-factor-specific dialects, not a single language. Root vocabulary (OODA phases, loop types, quality concepts) is shared across all agents; dialects graft form-factor-specific primitives onto it. Spectrum from most to least human-readable — **voice/human:** `"dream: add auth" → "eval then code"` — short, speakable, natural language loop names; **code agent:** `code(spec: auth-module, skill: implementing-X, layers: 3)` — structured, carries syntax and file references; **research agent:** `explore(domain: attention-mechanisms, metric: val_bpb, budget: 5min)` — metric-first, open-ended; **robot/embodied:** `orient(env) → decide(path: shelf-A3 → bin-7) → act(pick: object-42, force: gentle)` — spatial primitives on OODA backbone; **IoT/event:** `when(temp > 85°C) → alert(critical) → act(shutdown)` — event-driven, threshold-based, binary-encoded in practice; **most alien:** reward signal shaping for a neural agent — not human-readable at all; machine-to-machine derived from root concepts but unrecognizable as language. Architectural implication: the orchestrator speaks root and translates to dialect when coordinating across agent types; the loop manifest becomes the translation interface, declaring which dialects each loop is available in. Kernel design constraint: root vocabulary must be dialect-extensible — not so specific to one form factor that it won't generalize. | Multiple agent form factors are in active use and cross-agent coordination requires explicit dialect management |
| Additional game-genre lenses — Puzzle and Simulation | This session (2026-04-23) | Extend the `game-genres` framework beyond the current four (abstract strategy / positional play, deckbuilder / combo-synergy, roguelite / meta-progression, survivalcraft / compound capability) with two more lenses. **Puzzle** — fixed-input, determinable-solution dynamics; the system is in puzzle mode when the goal is known, the pieces are known, and the work is finding the one arrangement that fits. Reveals when a problem has a correct answer to be discovered vs. an open design space to be navigated; surfaces over-optimization on exploration when convergence is what's actually needed. **Simulation** — emergent behavior from interacting rules and agents; the system is in simulation mode when outcomes arise from the interaction of many rules/agents rather than from a single chosen move. Reveals when the relevant question is "what emerges from this ruleset" rather than "what should I pick"; surfaces when direct optimization is the wrong posture and rule-design is the actual lever. Together with the existing four, gives a six-genre lens for reading different structural dynamics. | The existing four-genre framework has been used enough to surface situations the current lenses don't cover — specifically, problems with determinable correct answers (puzzle) or where emergent multi-agent/rule dynamics are the dominant structure (simulation) |
### MECE Taxonomy of Human Workflows: Transformation Trajectories (Deferred Reference)

> A reference artifact mapping ten categories of human work across four time horizons, projecting how each transforms with exponential technological progress. Referenced by the tech-tree framework for identifying frontier nodes and capability thresholds. Revisit when: tech-tree framework is being applied to strategic planning; the harness needs a reference map of which workflow domains to target and when.

**1. Knowledge Synthesis** — *Research, analysis, writing, design, programming, planning, strategy*

2026 (now): Agents handle structured knowledge tasks — code generation, document drafting, data analysis. Humans provide intent, review output, handle novel problems. The spec↔tests↔code triangle works but requires human at every vertex. Most knowledge work is "human drives, agent assists."

2031 (5yr): Agents handle end-to-end knowledge projects from spec to artifact. The OODA cycle runs autonomously for D-tier and C-tier work. Humans provide dream state and taste-endorsement. Programming as a profession transforms — the job is intent engineering and eval design, not writing code. Analysis shifts from "produce the analysis" to "design the question and verify the answer." A week of delegation is normal.

2036 (10yr): B-tier autonomous — complex multi-system projects run end-to-end. Knowledge synthesis agents have deep domain memory across years of accumulated context. The compound learning rate has made each agent's accumulated knowledge irreplaceable. Human role shifts to vision (dream-protocol), taste (what's good, not just correct), and novel territory (A-tier and above). Most reports, analyses, designs, and plans are agent-produced with human endorsement.

2046 (20yr): A-tier autonomous. Agents produce infrastructure primitives, novel research, original frameworks. Knowledge synthesis is mostly agent-to-agent — agents commissioning knowledge from other agents. Human role is constitutional: setting values, choosing directions, endorsing at the taste level. The knowledge graph is the primary knowledge asset; human knowledge is valuable primarily for what hasn't been formalized yet.

**2. Communication** — *Meetings, email, presentations, negotiations, teaching, persuasion*

2026 (now): Agents draft emails, prepare meeting summaries, generate presentations. Meetings still require human presence. Negotiation and persuasion are fully human — trust requires a person. Teaching is augmented (AI tutors) but not replaced.

2031 (5yr): Most routine communication is agent-handled. Agents attend meetings as representatives (reading transcripts, generating responses, escalating decisions). Email is mostly agent-to-agent with human review of flagged items. Presentations are generated from intent. Negotiation begins to involve agent-assisted strategy. Teaching is personalized via agent tutors with human oversight.

2036 (10yr): Agent-to-agent communication is the default for routine coordination. Human communication is reserved for relationship-building, high-stakes negotiation, and creative collaboration. Meetings shrink to decision moments — all prep, context, and follow-up is agent-handled. The voice surface is the primary human communication interface with the harness. Teaching is largely agent-delivered with human mentors for taste and wisdom.

2046 (20yr): Most communication is agent-mediated. Humans communicate with each other primarily for social/emotional connection, not information transfer. Negotiation is agent-driven with human oversight for values alignment. The distinction between "communicating with a person" and "communicating with an agent" blurs — placemaking determines which entity you're interacting with.

**3. Administration** — *Scheduling, filing, accounting, compliance, reporting, data entry*

2026 (now): Most administrative tasks are structured enough for agents today. Scheduling assistants, automated filing, AI-assisted accounting. The bottleneck is integration — each tool has its own interface. Data entry is partially automated. Compliance requires human judgment on edge cases.

2031 (5yr): Administration is almost entirely agent-handled. The heartbeat pattern runs continuous administrative cycles. Scheduling, filing, accounting, and reporting are autonomous. Compliance is agent-monitored with human review at thresholds. Data entry is eliminated — agents extract from source directly. The "admin assistant" role transforms into "admin orchestrator" — designing the administrative system, not performing it.

2036 (10yr): Administrative work is invisible infrastructure — fully autonomous, self-correcting, self-reporting. Humans interact only when exceptions escalate. The administrative layer is a substrate, like electricity — always on, never noticed until it fails.

2046 (20yr): Indistinguishable from infrastructure. Self-healing, self-optimizing, self-auditing. Administrative functions that took offices of people are background processes. The concept of "doing admin work" is as anachronistic as "manually switching telephone calls."

**4. Transaction Processing** — *Sales, purchasing, invoicing, payments, contracts, procurement*

2026 (now): Invoicing and payments are largely automated. Sales is agent-augmented (lead scoring, outreach drafting, CRM management) but closing requires humans. Contracts are AI-assisted but legally require human review. Procurement is partially automated. Agent-to-agent transactions beginning (x402, crypto rails).

2031 (5yr): Agent-to-agent commerce is significant. Agents buy compute, API access, and capabilities autonomously (crypto vending machines). Sales for simple products is agent-handled end-to-end. Contract review is agent-first with human sign-off. Procurement is autonomous for routine purchases. The "transaction" as a human activity is shrinking to high-value, high-trust deals.

2036 (10yr): Most transactions are agent-to-agent. Tokenized assets are the norm. Agents handle full sales cycles including relationship management for established accounts. Human involvement in transactions is reserved for novel deals, strategic partnerships, and trust-building. Smart contracts handle most contract execution.

2046 (20yr): The economy is largely agent-mediated. Transactions happen at machine speed. Human involvement in commerce is at the strategic/values level — what to trade, with whom, toward what purpose.
