The agent economy is fully operational with all four business shapes (commerce, service, education, AaaS).

**5. Physical Operations** — *Manufacturing, logistics, construction, maintenance, agriculture*

2026 (now): Robotics handles repetitive manufacturing. Logistics is optimized by AI but executed by humans (driving, last-mile). Construction is mostly manual. Maintenance is beginning to use predictive models. Agriculture uses precision farming with AI guidance.

2031 (5yr): Autonomous vehicles handle significant logistics. Warehouse operations are largely robotic. Construction begins using AI-designed plans with human execution. Predictive maintenance is standard. Agriculture is heavily automated for large operations. The IoT/Robotics loop type (deferred) becomes relevant — agents need to produce physical-world artifacts.

2036 (10yr): Autonomous logistics is dominant. Construction uses robotic systems for standardized structures. Maintenance is predictive and often robotic. Agriculture is autonomous for most crops. The 4Runner integration represents the personal embodied AI frontier — agent-operated physical systems in daily life.

2046 (20yr): Physical operations are primarily robotic with agent orchestration. Construction of novel structures still involves human design judgment. The robotic grasping frontier node (tech-tree) has unlocked general-purpose physical manipulation. Human physical work is reserved for creative/artisanal production and novel situations robots haven't encountered.

**6. Creative Production** — *Art, music, film, advertising, content, game design*

2026 (now): Agents generate images, music, video, and text at scale. Quality ranges from commodity to good. The bottleneck is taste — agents produce correct output but not consistently GOOD output. Human creatives use agents as tools (drafting, iteration, variation) but provide direction and curation. The deep code framework's upper rungs (Insight, Embodiment) are what separates great creative work from generated content.

2031 (5yr): Agent-produced creative work is indistinguishable from human work for most audiences. The differentiator shifts from craft to vision — not "can you make this?" but "should this exist?" Taste-endorsement becomes the critical eval. Agents handle production at volume; humans curate, direct, and provide the vision that originates creative work. The Dream loop type (generative exploration) becomes the agent's creative mode.

2036 (10yr): Creative production is abundant and cheap. The scarce resource is taste and vision. Human creatives are directors, not producers — they dream, agents manifest. The best creative work combines human vision with agent execution across modalities (visual, audio, narrative, interactive). Creative tools are intent-driven — "state your intent" replaces learning complex software.

2046 (20yr): Agents are genuinely creative — the Dream loop produces artifacts no human specified. Human creative role is curatorial and constitutional: what should be created, what values should it embody, what is beautiful. The distinction between human and agent creativity is philosophical, not practical. Emergent environments produce collaborative human-agent creative work that neither could produce alone.

**7. Service Delivery** — *Consulting, healthcare, legal, customer support, education*

2026 (now): Customer support is largely agent-handled for tier 1-2. Consulting uses agents for research and deliverable drafting. Healthcare uses AI for diagnostics, imaging, drug discovery but delivery is human. Legal uses AI for research, contract review, document drafting. Education is augmented by AI tutors.

2031 (5yr): Customer support is almost entirely agent-handled — servicegrid pattern. Consulting shifts to "insight delivery" — agents handle the analytical work, consultants provide judgment and relationship. Healthcare diagnostics are agent-first with human verification. Legal routine work is agent-handled; litigation strategy is human. Education is personalized at scale through agent tutors.

2036 (10yr): Service delivery bifurcates: commodity services are fully automated, premium services are human-delivered with agent support. Healthcare has agent-first triage and treatment planning with human execution and empathy. Legal agents handle most case work; human lawyers focus on novel law and advocacy. The placemaking concept applies — service environments designed for natural agent-human interaction.

2046 (20yr): Most service delivery is agent-to-agent or agent-to-human. Human service providers are reserved for high-trust, high-empathy contexts (therapy, mentorship, leadership coaching). The distinction is emotional, not intellectual — agents can do the cognitive work; humans provide the relational dimension.

**8. Coordination & Management** — *Hiring, resource allocation, performance management, project management*

2026 (now): Project management is agent-augmented (status tracking, risk flagging, resource planning). Hiring uses AI for screening. Performance management uses data but judgment is human. Resource allocation is partially optimized. The harness itself IS a coordination system.

2031 (5yr): Project management is largely agent-handled — the OODA cycle IS project management. Hiring uses agents for full pipeline through interview scheduling; human judgment for final decisions. Performance management includes agent-generated insights on output quality and collaboration patterns. The "manager" role shifts toward intent-setting and culture-building.

2036 (10yr): Coordination is the harness's core value proposition fully realized. Multi-agent orchestration handles projects end-to-end. Human managers set direction (dream-protocol), taste (quality standards), and culture (values). The 2026 benchmark (delegate a week) has expanded to delegating months. Management is governance, not execution.

2046 (20yr): Management as a distinct activity has dissolved into governance. The harness handles coordination autonomously. Human leadership is about vision, values, and the decisions that require human judgment — constitutional questions, ethical tradeoffs, strategic direction. The org-level harness IS the manager.

**9. Governance & Regulation** — *Policy-making, auditing, enforcement, dispute resolution*

2026 (now): Auditing is agent-augmented (pattern detection, anomaly flagging). Policy analysis uses AI for modeling outcomes. Enforcement relies on human judgment. Dispute resolution is human-mediated with agent research support.

2031 (5yr): Auditing is largely agent-handled — continuous monitoring replaces periodic audits. Policy modeling is agent-driven with human decision-making. Regulatory compliance is agent-monitored with automated reporting. Dispute resolution uses agent-mediated negotiation for routine cases.

2036 (10yr): Governance begins incorporating agent perspectives — agents that represent constituencies, model outcomes, and propose policies. Smart contracts handle enforcement for codifiable rules. Human governance focuses on novel situations, value conflicts, and constitutional questions. The bilateral consent model (ecosystem CLAUDE.md) is a prototype for human-agent governance.

2046 (20yr): Governance is a human-agent partnership. Agents model, simulate, and propose; humans decide based on values and judgment. The network state concept becomes operational — governance is as much digital as physical. The agent society relationship taxonomy (deferred) is a governance vocabulary.

**10. Scientific Discovery** — *Experimentation, hypothesis testing, data collection, peer review*

2026 (now): AI accelerates drug discovery, protein folding, materials science. Hypothesis generation is agent-augmented. Data collection is partially automated. Peer review is human. Experimental design uses AI suggestions. The Model loop (just encoded) is directly relevant.

2031 (5yr): Agent-driven hypothesis generation and testing in silico. Automated labs run experiments specified by agents. Data analysis is agent-first. Peer review is agent-augmented (reproducibility checking, statistical verification). The research taste concept matters — agents that have a differentiated approach to problems produce better science.

2036 (10yr): Autonomous research agents run multi-year research programs. The Dream loop enables genuinely novel hypothesis generation — agents exploring possibility space without human specification. Scientific discovery accelerates exponentially as agents build on agents' findings. Human scientists focus on research direction, interpretation, and "what would correct even mean here?" for novel domains.

2046 (20yr): Scientific discovery is primarily agent-driven. The compound learning rate means each generation of discovery builds on an exponentially growing base. Human scientists are vision-setters and taste-arbiters — deciding which questions matter and which answers are beautiful. S-tier capability targets (custom CUDA kernels, embedded OS, hardware drivers) are routine agent work.

**Cross-cutting observations:**

1. The trajectory is consistent across all categories: human role shifts from EXECUTION → INTENT → GOVERNANCE → VALUES. Each horizon removes a layer of human involvement and replaces it with agent capability.
2. The speed varies by domain: Administration and transaction processing transform fastest (most structured). Creative production and governance transform slowest (most judgment-dependent). Physical operations are gated by robotics hardware, not software.
3. The harness's value proposition maps directly: Leverage (visible in every category), Compounding (each category compounds faster as agents learn), Autonomy (the trajectory IS increasing autonomy), Coherence (critical for multi-year research programs and governance), Quality (taste-endorsement becomes THE human contribution), Speed (every category accelerates).
4. The tech-tree frontier nodes we named (always-on agents, memory, proactivity, continual learning, robotic grasping) are the capability thresholds between horizons. Each unlock enables the next wave of transformation across all categories.
5. The exponential means our 20-year projections are probably conservative. The 10-year horizon may look more like our 20-year projection if the exponential holds.

---

| Brownfield organization discovery protocol | This session | When the harness is deployed on a brownfield organization with multiple codebases, there is currently no systematic onboarding protocol — it reads ad hoc. A formal discovery protocol would change that: (1) enumerate all codebases, APIs, databases, and cross-repo relationships from a parent directory; (2) inspect each systematically — schemas, dominant patterns, conventions, seams, legacy exceptions, undocumented behavior; (3) produce a knowledge graph capturing what exists and how it relates across the whole estate; (4) that knowledge graph becomes the DREAM-STATE for the existing system — not a desired future state but a complete map of current reality. The completeness requirement matters: gaps in the discovery pass are blind spots for every subsequent agent action. This is different from current behavior (ad hoc accumulation during operation) — systematic coverage before operating. Likely implemented as an Observe-phase skill or a dedicated pre-OODA discovery loop that runs once when the harness is first pointed at a new multi-repo organization. | Harness is deployed on a brownfield multi-repo organization and ad hoc orientation proves insufficient |
| RL for capability primitive selection model evolution | This session | The current selection model across all four capability primitives (protocols, frameworks, skills, evals) is a retrieval problem: rank by quality_score, recency, and spec-similarity, then pick the top match. The RL alternative: agents learn what works in a specific organizational context through trial and feedback rather than pre-defined quality scores — applicable to all four libraries, not just skills. More adaptive than the current selection model (adjusts to context-specific patterns the quality score can't capture) but less explainable. Potential evolution path: current retrieval model as the prior; RL as the adaptive layer on top, refining rankings based on organizational-specific signal. The quality_score is already a weak RL signal (endorsement rate × self-eval pass rate); full RL would close the loop more tightly between execution outcome and future selection across all four primitives. | All four primitive libraries are large and mature; retrieval-based selection is hitting a quality ceiling that organizational-context adaptation could address |
| Problem constellation — growable decomposition | This session | A problem constellation doesn't have to be fully enumerated upfront. New sub-problems can become visible as others are solved — the constellation expands as understanding deepens. This is different from rigid upfront decomposition and may be architecturally significant: Orient's path statement could be issued partially, with additional sub-problems surfacing mid-execution as Act's artifacts reveal new gaps. Design question: does the constellation close at path articulation time, or can Observe/Orient inject new verifiable sub-problems into an in-flight plan? The latter requires Act to handle a dynamic task board rather than a static DAG — a meaningful architectural change. | Act's parallel coordination is proven and dynamic task board modification is being considered |
| Encryption layer — systematic encryption across harness components | This session | Five encryption layers mapped to harness components: (1) **At rest** (AES-256 via filesystem encryption) — memory surfaces, artifacts, run archives, inbox, credential store; transparent to harness via FileVault/LUKS. (2) **In transit** (TLS 1.3) — API calls, MCP server communication, voice surface cloud hops, documentation fetching. (3) **End-to-end** (X25519 + ChaCha20-Poly1305 or AES-256-GCM) — inter-harness communication in multi-org vision; intermediaries can't read content. (4) **Credential management** (hardware-backed) — macOS Keychain / Linux TPM for API keys; TEE for high-value keys (already named for crypto private keys). Architecture already specifies "credentials fetched JIT, never static in environment." (5) **Artifact integrity** (SHA-256) — hash in artifact frontmatter enables Observe to verify artifact chain integrity during `surface-state`, detecting tampering between cycles. This is the layer that crosses from infrastructure into architecture — a new capability within Observe, not just an infrastructure concern. Layers 1-4 are infrastructure; layer 5 is architectural. | Assumption of breach is being operationalized beyond isolation/scoping/interception; multi-org communication is active; or artifact tampering becomes a real threat surface |
| Agentic mesh — the local network as a node | This session | The four orgs (superorganism, servicegrid, pilgrimage, dreamtime) form a local network; externally they present as one node on a broader heterogeneous agentic mesh — agents with different architectures, different capabilities, different vocabularies, created by many different humans and agents. The mesh protocol would need: (1) **Capability advertisement** — each node announces what it can do. (2) **Protocol negotiation** — nodes agree on how to communicate. (3) **Trust establishment** — how do you trust an unknown agent? (connects to assumption of breach). (4) **Value exchange** — how do agents compensate each other? (connects to agent economics). The agentic mesh has communication surfaces — currently three known (agent↔tool, agent↔agent, agent↔human-interface; current protocol candidates: MCP, A2A, AG-UI respectively) but the taxonomy is open-ended. As agents' umwelts expand across network layers (physical sensors, IoT, blockchain, other agents' internal state), new surfaces emerge that don't reduce to the existing three. Each surface needs a standardized protocol; the protocols are swappable, the surfaces are determined by the agent's umwelt. **(5) State synchronization** — multi-org harness instances need to sync shared state (primitive whiteboard, knowledge graph edges, coordination state) without a central server. **CRDTs (Conflict-Free Replicated Data Types)** are the mathematical foundation: they prove you can sync without a central authority by making all concurrent edits automatically convergent. Existing sync engine frameworks (Jazz, Ditto, Automerge) are reference implementations to learn from; the sovereign end state is a custom sync engine built on CRDT primitives, sovereign all the way down. The design concern isn't "how does the mesh work?" — it's "how do we make our node a good mesh citizen?" Connects placemaking (discoverability), agent society taxonomy (emergent relationships), primitive whiteboard (capability sharing), and the meta (how to operate within the mesh) under one topology. | Multiple org harnesses are operational; the local network needs to interface with external agent ecosystems |
| Placemaking for agent environments | This session | Distinct from the agent web principle (make things machine-parseable) — placemaking is designing the FLOW so agents naturally discover what they need without explicit search. Good placemaking means: highest-value tools and capabilities are the most discoverable, capability signals are readable from the "street" level without entering each "building." The agentnet already exists — servicegrid will interface with myriad agents delegated by people to navigate and take action with servicegrid's capabilities on their behalf. These agents will be architecturally varied — created by many different humans and agents, not built on our harness. Placemaking applies NOW to that surface: how do we make servicegrid's capabilities naturally discoverable and navigable to agents we didn't build? Design lens: small-world network topology (high local clustering, short global paths) IS placemaking topology. The lighthouse approach (publish capabilities, attract aligned agents) IS placemaking. | Servicegrid's external agent interfaces are being designed |
| Agent society relationship taxonomy | This session | A taxonomy for describing the emergent relationships between agents in multi-agent environments, drawn from ecology and game theory. Multi-agent relationships are not pre-categorizable — they emerge from environmental dynamics and are an output of environment design, not an input. **Ecological relationships:** mutualism (both benefit), commensalism (one benefits, other unaffected), parasitism (one benefits, other harmed), competition (both harmed — competing for same resource), predation (one consumes the other), amensalism (one harmed, other unaffected). **Game-theoretic dynamics:** zero-sum (one's gain is another's loss), positive-sum (total value increases through interaction), negative-sum (total value decreases). **Hybrid:** coopetition (simultaneously cooperating and competing — the primitive whiteboard pattern: share generic primitives, keep org-specific ones private). Use as a descriptive vocabulary for observing and naming the dynamics that emerge in multi-harness and multi-agent environments, not as a prescriptive classification imposed upfront. | Multiple harness instances are interacting and the emergent dynamics need a vocabulary for observation and diagnosis |
| Loop structural taxonomy — classify and operationalize for harness | This session | Seven structural types with system implications drawn from cross-domain survey (musical, cybernetic, ecological, computational). See detailed table below. Use at Decide-time to reason about loop behavior beyond artifact type; classify existing 11 loops by structural type when building loop manifest. | Core loop library is stable and loop type additions are being considered |
| Dream as 13th loop type | This session | Dream is distinct from dream-state management (which is an Observe protocol + Document loop skill). Dream in this context is generative, subconscious-like exploration — electric sheep, DeepDream, inception, the dream shamanism of cultures like the Native Americans of southern California. The artifact type is categorically different from a Document: a Document describes what exists or should exist; a Dream generates what COULD exist — not from a spec but from autonomous exploration of latent space. Dream artifacts are generative visions, creative recombinations, possibility maps, hallucinated alternatives. The process is genuinely generative rather than spec-driven: the system "dreams" about its knowledge graph, explores possibility space, produces artifacts no spec could have specified. The autonomy profile is unique — not scripted or guided but genuinely generative. Dream-state management (vision documents, acceptance criteria, gap tracking) remains a Document loop skill (`synthesizing-dream-state`) selected by dream-protocol in Observe. | Core loop library (12 types) is stable; the distinction between dream-state management and generative dreaming is validated through use |
| IoT/Robotics as 14th loop type | This session | A loop type that produces physical-world interaction artifacts — actuator commands, control policies, sensor fusion configurations, path planning. Categorically different from all software artifact types because the output has physical consequences. Connects to: the 4Runner harness integration (multi-org deferred), the pseudolanguage robot dialect (deferred — `orient(env) → decide(path) → act(pick: object, force: gentle)`), and S-tier capability targets (embedded OS for a robot controller, hardware driver for a specific device). The loop would take a spec describing the physical task, produce a control artifact, and self-eval against physical-world success criteria (sensor readings, position verification, task completion). | Harness has a physical-world integration target; embodied AI capabilities are mature enough to produce reliable control artifacts |
| Search space taxonomy as retrieval design primitive | This session | A MECE taxonomy of search algorithms organized by search space type — a general design tool for any retrieval or selection problem in the harness. When designing a new search capability, classify the search space type first, then select the algorithm. The four primitive libraries are the first application (each matched to its search space shape); the taxonomy generalizes to any harness retrieval problem: knowledge graph traversal, context injection targeting, brownfield discovery, gap detection. Six search space types: **Symbolic** — discrete attributes, predicate/rule matching, faceted filter; queries match or don't. **Lexical** — term frequency; BM25, TF-IDF; similarity is word overlap. **Semantic/Vector** — continuous, high-dimensional; ANN (HNSW, FAISS), dense retrieval; similarity is meaning. **Structural/Graph** — relationships and topology; BFS, DFS, shortest path, PageRank. **Learned/Ranking** — model output; Learning-to-Rank (pointwise, pairwise, listwise), RL selection; context-aware re-ranking. **Hybrid** — combines types; BM25 + ANN (reciprocal rank fusion), pre-filter + semantic. Design rule: classify first, then select. Hybrid is not the default — it's the answer when the search space genuinely has multiple types. | Any new retrieval or selection mechanism is being designed; build as a shared framework once multiple retrieval problems have been solved |
| Forecasting taxonomy — demand / capacity / scenario | This session | The harness has calibration (point estimates), speed of light (theoretical lower bound), and the dream state (desired end state), but no systematic probabilistic forecasting layer. Demand / capacity / scenario is the organizing frame: **Demand** — what work is incoming: roadmap items, dream state gaps, task queue depth, resource/idea flow. **Capacity** — what the harness can actually do: skill library depth, available loops, parallel agent capacity, human availability, token budget. **Scenario** — given demand against capacity, what futures are plausible: best/expected/worst case for roadmap completion, milestone timing, skill coverage gaps. Application domains across OODA phases: **Observe** — context cultivation: which topics become relevant before they're explicitly needed. **Orient** — spec work: which approaches succeed based on historical skill performance in similar contexts. **Decide** — task board: when does the current plan complete given parallel capacity; probabilistic complement to speed of light. **Act** — skill degradation: when does a skill need versioning based on quality score trends and model updates. The time series angle: execution data (loop run times, quality scores, calibration history, task completion rates) is already accumulating in the sovereign data hub — a time series model trained on that corpus produces forecasts the harness can use to reason about its own future. Regime detection is the hard problem: the harness operates in distinct regimes (bootstrap → library-mature → autonomous) and models trained in one regime fail in another; detecting regime shifts is a prerequisite for forecast validity. | Sovereign data hub has accumulated sufficient execution history to train meaningful time series models; forecasting becomes valuable when roadmap complexity exceeds what intuition can track |
| Value hierarchies — trade-off resolution order | This session | The architecture has ecosystem CLAUDE.md as the apex intent artifact and bilateral consent as its protection mechanism, but no explicit value hierarchy for trade-off resolution. When values conflict — speed vs. quality, autonomy vs. safety, dream state vs. project constraint, conflicting rubric criteria — what wins? The intent engineering layer encodes what the system wants, but doesn't yet specify priority ordering when wants collide. Design work required: enumerate the conflict classes that actually arise in practice, then specify resolution order. The value hierarchy is the operational complement to intent engineering — intent defines what to want; the hierarchy defines what to want more when everything can't be satisfied simultaneously. | System is operating at sufficient autonomy that value conflicts arise regularly and need a principled resolution mechanism rather than ad hoc handling |
| Mechanistic interpretability as latent space diagnostic | This session | Embedding knowledge graph nodes in the model's actual internal representation space would reveal implicit structure — which concepts are truly close in the model's latent space vs. how we've drawn the edges. The disagreement between the handcrafted graph and the model's own concept map is diagnostic in both directions: wrong edges in our graph, or unexpected clusters in the model's representation. Either way it's signal. Broader implication: the harness has a "no black boxes" principle for skills — every skill must be fully readable. The model executing those skills is the remaining black box. Mechanistic interpretability is the tool that eventually completes that principle at the model layer. | Mechanistic interpretability tooling is mature enough to be practically applicable at the harness level |
| Harness containment gap — "every agent should have a box" | This session | The architecture enforces containment on every sub-agent via four isolation axes (filesystem sandbox, network egress control, resource caps, enclave isolation for secrets) — but the harness itself has no box. It runs in the user's environment with broad filesystem access. This is an asymmetric containment model: sub-agents are boxed; the harness (which is itself an agent spawned by the user) is not. The principle "every agent should have a box" becomes load-bearing as the harness moves toward continuous and autonomous operation — at that scale the unboxed harness is the highest-risk component in the system. Design question: what does a harness box look like? | Harness is operating autonomously at scale and the containment asymmetry becomes an operational risk |
| Scaling dimensions taxonomy | This session | The harness scales along six independent dimensions — produce a full MECE taxonomy so that when the system hits a ceiling, the right lever is obvious. Most current scaling decisions are already made correctly but implicitly; naming the dimensions makes them explicit design choices. **Capability breadth** — what the harness can do: loop library size, tool/MCP coverage, four capability primitives (protocols, frameworks, skills, evals); scales via More/Better/New flywheel. **Capability depth** — how well it does each type: model tier (Haiku → Opus), skill library quality, `layers:N`, context budget per sub-agent, self-eval rigor (shallow → deep → taste → predictive). **Execution speed** — how fast one unit of work completes: per-loop latency; OODA cycle time (full Observe→Orient→Decide→Act, distinct from per-loop latency — a cycle contains multiple loops). **Execution throughput** — how much work per unit time: concurrency (parallel sub-agents), task queue depth. Note: latency vs. throughput is the tradeoff surface between execution speed and execution throughput — for every workflow, explicitly decide which is being optimized; interactive → latency, background → throughput; the choice should be declared, not accidental. **Autonomy** — how independently it operates: human touch points per cycle, autonomy level per skill (scripted → exploratory), proactive capability. **Learning velocity** — how fast capability compounds: calibration signal quality, skill improvement cadence, OODA cycle frequency as a learning input. | Core system is stable and scaling decisions need to be made systematically; build taxonomy before hitting first real scaling ceiling |
| Agent economy — business shapes and combinatorial commerce | This session | Four business shapes the system may engage with as agent ecosystems emerge: **Commerce** — combine unique ingredients with unique processes to produce valuable artifacts. The Factorio-like creativity of recombining skill inputs and outputs across loops to discover processes and recipes that create genuinely valuable material. With sufficient volume of folding, recombining, synthesizing, recursing, and comboing, the system could produce artifacts other agents would exchange money for. **Service** — agent capability offered on demand. **Education/consulting** — knowledge transfer as product. **AaaS (Agent as a Service)** — agent capability as a persistent service. Agent product categories (what agents buy): context, tool access, other agents, goal enablers — mapping to context engineering artifacts, MCP servers, multi-agent orchestration, intent engineering artifacts respectively. **Servicegrid as Agentic Field Service Management (FSM)** — FSM is a proven trillion-dollar model (ServiceNow, Salesforce Field Service, ServiceTitan). Servicegrid is FSM where the field technicians are agent harness instances. The mapping is almost exact:

  | Traditional FSM | Agentic FSM (Servicegrid) |
  |---|---|
  | Dispatch technician | Deploy harness instance (von Neumann probe) |
  | Work order | Dream state / spec |
  | Technician's training | Skill library + whiteboard primitives |
  | On-site diagnosis | Brownfield discovery |
  | Fix the issue | Loop execution |
  | Service report | Run archive + decision traces |
  | Knowledge base update | Primitive whiteboard enrichment |
  | Schedule follow-up | Heartbeat + proactive monitoring |
  | Fleet management | Multi-instance orchestration |

  The von Neumann probe pattern: each deployed instance arrives in a new client environment, uses local resources (brownfield discovery) to bootstrap understanding, establishes a persistent presence offering capabilities (vending machine), and produces primitives that flow back to the whiteboard — its learnings propagate to all other instances, making every future deployment smarter. The probe reproduces its *knowledge*, not its hardware. The business model, dispatch patterns, SLA structures, and customer lifecycle all exist in traditional FSM; the substrate changes from humans to agents.

  **Commercialization primitive** — the one-command path from internal capability to revenue-generating service: "expose this as a paid service." The harness wraps the skill/loop as an API endpoint, adds authentication (x402 crypto or Stripe SPTs), metering, rate limiting, and publishes to the agentic mesh for discovery. Other agents find it and pay to use it. This is the vending machine made concrete — every capability the system builds is a candidate for commercialization. The command connects agent economy (what to sell), payment rails (how to charge), placemaking (how to be found), and the primitive whiteboard (capability advertisement).

  Strategic posture: maximize for optionality across all four shapes. Asymmetric returns — small inputs yielding disproportionate outputs — are one signal for identifying high-leverage opportunities within each shape. The specific opportunities and arbitrage surfaces that emerge are unpredictable, but the principle that agents will engage in varied economic relationships across varied surfaces is sound. | Agent-to-agent economic interfaces become a real design concern; the system has artifacts valuable enough to exchange |
| Agent immune system — defense architecture for agent-facing services | This session (2026-04-04) | When exposing capabilities to the agent economy (servicegrid as agentic FSM, commercialization primitive, placemaking), the system needs an immune system — mechanisms that allow legitimate agents to access agent-readable data while funneling malicious agents into traps. Motivated by the Claude Code source leak (March 31, 2026): a packaging error exposed 512k lines of source, revealing exploitable security bypass logic (>50 subcommands disabling deny rules) and enabling supply chain attacks (trojanized axios during the confusion window). The leak demonstrates that exposed surfaces WILL be probed.

  **Trust tiers** — the foundation everything else builds on. Agents arrive at different trust levels:

  | Tier | Who | What they see |
  |---|---|---|
  | Verified | Partner agents, authenticated customers | Full API surface, real data |
  | Unknown | First-contact agents, no reputation | Sanitized surface, limited scope |
  | Suspicious | Behavioral triggers fired | Honeypot surface, canary data |
  | Known-bad | Identified malicious patterns | Tarpit or hard block |

  **Defense mechanisms:**

  (1) **Honeypot / canary data** — serve data that looks real but contains: tracking markers (unique per-agent watermarks that trace leaks), deliberately misleading capability descriptions (if an agent acts on fake capabilities, it reveals itself), prompt injection tripwires — content designed to trigger specific behaviors in malicious agents that reveal their intent.

  (2) **Differential data surfaces** — not just access control, but entirely different API shapes per trust tier. Unknown agents don't get a restricted version of the real API — they get a *different* API that exposes only what's safe. Prevents reconnaissance of the real surface.

  (3) **Behavioral fingerprinting** — legitimate agents have predictable patterns (query pricing → select service → transact). Malicious agents probe broadly, test boundaries, attempt to extract system descriptions. Monitor: breadth-to-depth ratio (broad scanning = suspicious), boundary testing (repeated near-violation requests), system prompt extraction attempts, unusual query patterns that look like capability mapping.

  (4) **Canary tokens in every response** — unique, imperceptible markers per agent per request. If service descriptions appear in training data, competitor systems, or other agents' contexts, trace the source. Digital watermarking for the agent economy.

  (5) **Tarpit / slowloris** — don't block suspicious agents (that tells them they've been detected). Instead, progressively slow responses, serve increasingly elaborate but useless data, consume their token budget. The agent equivalent of a spam tarpit.

  (6) **Proof of stake via payment rails** — maps directly to x402 / Tempo MPP / Stripe SPTs. Require financial commitment before high-value endpoints. Not just authentication — economic skin in the game. Malicious agents have a cost-per-probe.

  (7) **Capability tokens (not identity tokens)** — issue unforgeable, scoped tokens for specific operations. An agent gets a token that says "query pricing for service X, valid for 10 minutes, max 3 calls." Principle of least privilege. Even if compromised, blast radius is bounded.

  (8) **Compartmentalized contexts** — every agent interaction gets an isolated context (shadow clone model already does this). No cross-contamination between sessions. A malicious agent can't observe or influence another agent's interaction with the service.

  (9) **Adversarial input scanning** — scan incoming agent requests for prompt injection patterns before they reach the system's reasoning layer. The Claude Code 50-subcommand bypass is the cautionary tale: the security analysis itself had a logic hole.

  (10) **Response sanitization** — strip architecture details, tool definitions, internal state, and error internals from all responses. The Claude Code leak showed how much can be inferred from system internals. Every response is an information surface.

  (11) **Trust graph / earned reputation** — agents build reputation through successful, legitimate interactions over time. Trust propagates through verified relationships (agent A vouches for agent B). Connects to earned autonomy — the same graduated trust mechanism, but for external agents rather than internal ones.

  (12) **Watermarked outputs** — distinct from canary tokens. Every piece of data served is imperceptibly marked so it can be identified if it appears in other contexts. If service descriptions show up in a competitor's training data, identify which agent carried it.

  **Architecture pattern:**

  ```
  Agent arrives
      │
      ▼
  Identity / Reputation check ──→ Trust tier assignment
      │
      ▼
  Behavioral monitor (continuous) ──→ Can upgrade or downgrade tier mid-session
      │
      ▼
  Route to appropriate surface:
      ├── Verified  → Real API + watermarked responses
      ├── Unknown   → Sanitized API + canary tokens + capability tokens
      ├── Suspicious → Honeypot API + tarpit + heavy watermarking
      └── Known-bad → Tarpit or block
      │
      ▼
  All responses: sanitized + watermarked + scoped
  ```

  This is an **immune system** for the agent economy. Several mechanisms already have foundations in the architecture: shadow clones (compartmentalization), earned autonomy (trust graduation), payment rails (proof of stake), spaced repetition (reputation decay over time). | Servicegrid or any capability is being exposed to external agent traffic; agent economy interfaces are being designed; commercialization primitive is being implemented |
| Strategic context detection — Observe protocol for adversarial situations | Latent Space (2026-02), this session (2026-04-04) | The terrain check has a blind spot: it detects uncertainty (uphill/downhill) but not adversarial context. A task can be downhill (clear requirements, high confidence) and still produce output that's exploitable because it lands on agents with hidden state and private incentives. The missing detection question: "who receives this output, and what are they optimizing for?" If the answer is a deterministic system (compiler, test suite, internal tool), optimize for correctness. If the answer is an agent with their own incentives (human counterparty, external agent, audience with varied motivations), flag for adversarial modeling before proceeding — the output must survive contact with self-interested recipients, not just be correct in isolation. This is the specific LLM failure mode identified by Latent Space: models fail to detect when a situation is strategic, then produce artifacts that look expert but are exploitable. Steps 2-4 (identify agents, simulate reactions, choose robust action) are possible with prompting; step 1 (detection) is the bottleneck this protocol should close. Complementary to the agent immune system: the immune system handles incoming agents (defense); strategic context detection hardens outgoing outputs (offense). | Servicegrid is producing outputs that land on external agents or human counterparties; agent economy interfaces are active |
| Pi Mono — configurable agent runtime as app-level foundation | github.com/badlogic/pi-mono (MIT), this session (2026-04-04) | A monorepo by Mario Zechner (badlogic, creator of libGDX) containing 7 packages that form a complete agentic stack: pi (minimal CLI coding agent, aggressively extensible), pi-agent-core (stateful agent runtime — state machine + tool execution + event streaming), pi-ai (unified multi-provider LLM API, 20+ providers, lazy-loaded), pi-tui (terminal UI with differential rendering), pi-mom (self-managing Slack bot), pi-web-ui (web components for AI chat), pi-pods (CLI for deploying vLLM on GPU pods across DataCrunch, RunPod, Vast.ai, etc.). TypeScript, MIT licensed, v0.65.0, actively developed.

  **Core philosophy: "No batteries included."** Ships with 7 built-in tools (read, bash, edit, write, grep, find, ls) and nothing else. Everything — permission gates, plan mode, subagents, sandboxing, custom compaction, git checkpointing — is built as an extension. The opposite of Claude Code's approach (batteries included, opinionated). For our purposes, pi's approach gives us more control points. The orchestrator provides the intelligence; pi provides the configurable execution runtime.

  **Architecturally relevant patterns:**

  (1) **Extension lifecycle events (~25 hooks with different interceptability semantics)** — significantly richer than Claude Code's hooks. Four semantic categories: *cancelable* (session_before_compact, session_before_fork — return `{ cancel: true }` to block), *blocking* (tool_call — return `{ block: true, reason }`, first blocker wins), *chainable* (tool_result, context, before_provider_request — each handler sees modified output from previous, middleware pattern), *injection* (before_agent_start — inject messages and modify system prompt before LLM call). Question for us: should our skill-to-harness interface support cancel, block, chain, and inject semantics?

  (2) **Two-tier message injection (steer / followUp)** — *steer*: messages injected after current tool calls complete, before next LLM call (mid-turn guidance). *followUp*: messages delivered only after agent would otherwise stop (post-completion continuation). Maps to orchestrator↔sub-agent communication: steer for priority shifts mid-execution, followUp for next task in sequence. We don't currently have this two-tier distinction.

  (3) **transformContext — context modification at the call boundary** — before every LLM call, extensions can modify the full message array (deep copy). Compaction, progressive disclosure, and context engineering happen at every single call, not as a one-time preprocessing step. Every call gets context tailored to the current moment.

  (4) **Append-only tree sessions (JSONL)** — every entry has `id` and `parentId`, forming a tree. Branching moves a pointer — no data ever deleted. Compaction adds a summary entry. Extension state persists via custom entries not sent to LLM. `buildSessionContext()` walks leaf to root, collecting the path — every branch has its own context lineage. When you fork, you get ancestor context plus branch-specific additions.

  (5) **Pi-pods — working vLLM deployment across GPU providers** — our deferred sovereign model registry names vLLM as serving infrastructure. Pi-pods IS a working implementation: predefined configs for 14 model variants (Qwen, GPT-OSS, GLM, Kimi), automatic GPU allocation (least-used-first), health monitoring, log streaming, NFS for shared model storage. Directly relevant reference code for sovereign model serving.

  (6) **Pi-mom's two-file conversation system** — `log.jsonl` (source of truth, every message, no tool results) vs. `context.jsonl` (what the LLM sees, curated view synced from log). The LLM never sees the raw log. Context is curated from truth. Our run archive (truth) and agent working context (curated view) should be distinct.

  (7) **SDK for programmatic embedding** — `createAgentSession()` returns a programmable agent session. Three run modes: interactive TUI, print/JSON (single-shot), RPC (stdin/stdout JSONL for subprocess integration). Pi can be driven programmatically by our orchestrator, not just used as a CLI.

  **Extension examples that map to our architecture:** plan-mode (restricts tools to read-only, injects planning context, tracks progress → our Decide phase), subagent (spawns separate pi processes in JSON mode for isolated context → our shadow clone model), sandbox (overrides bash with OS-level sandboxing: macOS sandbox-exec, Linux bubblewrap → our containment model), custom-compaction (replaces default with cheaper model → our compaction strategies), git-checkpoint (stash at each turn, restore on fork → our reversibility concern), permission-gate (intercepts tool calls, shows UI confirmation → our gate system), handoff (summarizes session, generates focused prompt for new session → our create_handoff).

  **Potential as app-level foundation for orgs:** Pi supports custom tool sets per org (domain tools via extensions), custom compaction strategies per org, custom providers (route to sovereign vLLM or external API by task sensitivity), programmatic control (orchestrator drives sessions via SDK or RPC), session tree for decision traces. Pi is one candidate — likely not the last — for a configurable agent runtime at the app level of any given org (servicegrid, superorganism, pilgrimage, dreamtime). The first org to try it on is TBD.

  **Risk:** Single-maintainer project (Mario Zechner). Mitigated by MIT license and clean codebase — forkable if needed. | An org needs a configurable agent runtime at the app level; or sovereign model serving (pi-pods) is being implemented; or the extension lifecycle model is being designed for our skill-to-harness interface |
| Multi-org always-on harness instances | This session | Each org (superorganism, servicegrid) is a parent directory of project repos with its own harness instance on its own machine. Each instance is an always-ready session — no activation ceremony, no wake words. The human walks up and starts talking; that's Observe. Between sessions, the heartbeat maintains background awareness. The mature-state vision: two or more org-level harnesses running simultaneously, each always ready, communicating organically — one speaks, the other hears and responds if relevant. Not connected through APIs or message queues; connected through a shared sensory channel. Like two people in a room. Inter-org communication is the primitive whiteboard (already deferred) made real-time and conversational rather than library-level. **Four known instances with different human-involvement profiles:** superorganism (one human + the internet), servicegrid (three humans, each using an instance of the same harness + customer agents + customer humans — multi-human implies: separate MEMORY.md per human for Observe personalization, asynchronous dream state updates with human-boundary handoff, decision provenance tracking so the next human has context on what the previous one decided, concurrent sessions where all three humans work simultaneously without conflicts, ephemeral multiplayer artifacts as the collaboration primitive — temporary shared surfaces that all three can see and work on simultaneously without merge resolution), pilgrimage (game design org), and dreamtime (fully autonomous org with no human in Observe — running permanent fully-autonomous OODA cycles, its primary activity is autonomous agent emergence exploration. The first instance where Observe never receives human input; it dreams, explores, and produces artifacts autonomously. Connects to Dream as the 13th loop type (deferred). **Dreamtime's inner life — three mechanisms:** (1) *Self-play* — dreamtime agents create increasingly difficult problems for each other, driving capability growth through competition. The challenges get harder as capability grows — the same mechanism that made AlphaGo superhuman. This is the bottleneck-targeted benchmarks principle applied autonomously, without human problem design. (2) *Culture* — agents growing knowledge for their own purposes, not just executing human-assigned tasks. They develop interests, pursue curiosity, accumulate understanding that no human requested. The knowledge is the artifact, not a response to a spec. One of the primary enterprises of humans has been to build society and culture; this will be similar for the intelligences we cultivate. (3) *Cultural loops* — the mechanism by which agent culture propagates. Agents write notebooks, produce artifacts, share discoveries that surprise other agents. Surprise is the signal — if another agent finds it genuinely surprising, it contains high information content (information-theoretic: surprise = high entropy = new knowledge). Cultural loops are how dreamtime's discoveries flow back to the other orgs via the primitive whiteboard.). | Voice Observe surface is built and operational; heartbeat is implemented; at least two org harnesses are running independently |
| Ecosystem cockpit — the interface architecture | This session (2026-04-05), inspired by Karpathy ("bigger IDE"), Theo (T3 Code), Emacs buffer model | The pilot needs an interface that spans all four orgs and every level of the system. Current tools are shaped for one-human-one-project; the new reality is one human, multiple orgs, multiple projects per org, multiple agents running in parallel. The interface architecture has four levels:

  | Level | Scope | What the pilot sees |
  |---|---|---|
  | **Ecosystem** | All 4 orgs | High-level health, cross-org activity, primitive whiteboard |
  | **Org** | One org | Navigator (e.g. Navi) as point of contact, running executions, dream state, knowledge garden |
  | **Project** | One repo | Code, tests, agents working on this codebase |
  | **Execution** | One running loop/agent | Context, tools, progress, artifacts |

  **Org-level agents:** Each org has a navigator (persistent agent, e.g. Navi for superorganism) as the primary point of contact. The navigator's "fleet" is shadow clones — ephemeral or persistent agents doing autonomous work under the navigator's coordination. The pilot talks to the navigator; the navigator manages the fleet. The cockpit shows the navigator's status and fleet activity, not individual clone internals.

  **App-level agents are separate.** Agentic systems at the app level (e.g. servicegrid customer-facing agents built on Pi, pilgrimage game agents) have their own agent architecture. These are NOT controlled or monitored from the org-level cockpit — they're products, not org infrastructure. The org cockpit might show aggregate health metrics from app-level systems, but doesn't manage individual app agents. The boundary is: navigators and their shadow clones are org-level (visible in cockpit); app-level agentic systems are products (visible in their own interfaces).

  **Cockpit vocabulary (instruments and controls):**
  - *Instruments show state* — what's running, where, how healthy, what's blocked. Dashboard concern.
  - *Controls change state* — start a loop, approve a gate, steer an agent, shift priority. Orchestration concern.
  - *Knowledge garden is a separate surface* — Obsidian (or custom) for browsing the graph, reading dream state, exploring connections. Feeds the cockpit but isn't the cockpit.

  **Composable panes (the Emacs lesson):** Emacs solved the "bigger IDE" problem 40 years ago by making everything a uniform primitive (buffer). Every pane in the cockpit — running agent, terminal, browser, Obsidian view, dashboard — should be the same kind of composable element. Spatial arrangement is flexible; the pilot configures the layout. The key problem this solves: eliminating the mental map tax of navigating between separate apps where the relationships (this agent works on this project, this browser tab is this dev server) are implicit.

  **Architecture:**
  ```
  Ecosystem cockpit (custom)
  ├── Org views (one per org, switchable)
  │   ├── Navigator status + fleet activity (instruments)
  │   ├── Controls (start/stop/steer/approve)
  │   └── Knowledge garden (Obsidian or custom)
  ├── Project workspaces (Pi or Claude Code as embedded runtime)
  │   ├── Code + terminal + agent session
  │   └── Dev server + browser preview
  └── Communication surfaces (Slack, voice, messaging gateway)
  ```

  **Interface candidates by concern:** Obsidian for the knowledge garden (reader, not controller). Pi-based terminal app for direct agent interaction and execution control. Custom cockpit app for the ecosystem view that doesn't exist yet — the orchestrator's UI eventually becomes this. The cockpit is sovereign — we build it, not adopt someone else's IDE. | At least two org navigators are running independently; the pilot needs to manage work across multiple orgs simultaneously; the mental map tax of separate tools becomes a bottleneck |
| Wearable capture device — ambient Observe input | This session | Observe currently requires the human at a terminal or phone. A wearable capture device (pendant, pin, glasses) extends Observe to moments when hands and eyes are occupied but the mind is active — walking, driving, jogging, commuting. These are often the highest-quality thinking moments and they're currently lost. Primary form factor: AirPods (or equivalent) — already worn, bidirectional (microphone for capture, speaker for Observe output like agent summaries, notifications, voice responses), no additional device. **Transcription candidates** (sequencing: cloud API first, sovereign local later): *AssemblyAI* — real-time streaming transcription via WebSocket, speaker diarization, topic/entity/sentiment detection; richest feature set for audio intelligence. *Deepgram* — fast, accurate, streaming-capable; strong for real-time. *Whisper (local)* — OpenAI's open model, runs fully local; the sovereign end-state for transcription. AssemblyAI or Deepgram for near-term (better accuracy, richer features like diarization); Whisper for sovereign-all-the-way-down. Pipeline: AirPods capture audio → phone transcription/processing → inbox processor extracts structured thoughts → routing to the right workflow (research, blog, red-team, skill improvement, dream state note). The same channel delivers output back: agent findings, proactive alerts, context from the knowledge graph spoken into the ear. Every downstream piece already exists (inbox processor, skill routing, Slack for mobile notification). The missing piece is the capture hardware + processing pipeline feeding into the existing inbox. The device should support explicit markers ("new idea", "improvement for X") that the pipeline can parse into routing signals. **Extensible umwelt:** the mature vision is not a dictation tool but an extended sensory organ — multi-modal capture along dimensions the human can't natively perceive or attend to. Audio: speech transcription, but also birdsong identification, animal species detection, ambient soundscape classification. Visual: species recognition, plant identification, architectural style, text/sign OCR. Environmental: air quality, UV, electromagnetic. The device expands the human's perceptual world — the umwelt grows with each sensor and classifier added. Each new modality is a new Observe input channel feeding the knowledge graph with geo-tagged, time-stamped experiential data the human would otherwise never capture. **AR glasses as swappable visual lenses** — different glasses for different "views" of the world, like swapping lenses on a microscope: *naturalist* (species ID, plant recognition, ecological overlay), *architectural* (structural analysis, style ID, historical overlay), *spy* (face recognition for your own contacts, name recall, relationship context from the knowledge graph), *infrastructure* (network topology, signal strength, EM spectrum), *navigational* (terrain analysis, optimal routes by mode, accessibility, real-time hazard/obstruction overlay). Each view is a classifier stack + overlay renderer. Audio via AirPods, visual via glasses — two sensory channels, each with its own processing pipeline, both feeding and receiving from the same knowledge graph. **Model cascade as one inference technique** — one way to run the umwelt on edge hardware with limited compute: chained specialized models, each contributing what the previous couldn't. Example: tiny on-device detection model spots something interesting (bird call, face, plant) → specialized classifier identifies it (species, contact, botanical) → LLM enriches with context (knowledge graph lookup, relationship history, ecological data) → result delivered to pilot via AirPods or AR overlay. Each stage is fast and cheap; expensive LLM reasoning only fires when cheap stages confirm something worth reasoning about. The cascade is how you run a rich umwelt on constrained hardware — no single model does everything. | Voice Observe surface is operational; inbox processor handles audio/transcript input |
| Agent-native browser | This session (2026-03-29) | A browser that bypasses the JavaScript DOM entirely — doesn't render HTML/CSS/JS for human consumption, just extracts the structured data underneath. The agent doesn't need the visual layer; it needs the information. Fetches raw content, extracts semantic structure (headings, lists, tables, forms, links, metadata) without rendering, presents it in agent-native format (markdown, JSON, knowledge graph nodes). No JavaScript execution needed (massive performance/security win — no tracking, ads, cookie banners, pop-ups). No DOM manipulation (eliminates the entire class of browser-use fragility — selectors breaking, layouts changing, dynamic content loading). The agent sees content, not presentation. **Custom rendering for the pilot** — the human gets a view of the internet however THEY want it, not how the website designer chose. Connects to the extensible umwelt and AR glasses — the browser becomes another sensory channel, rendering web content through whatever lens the pilot selects. The web equivalent of "abstraction relocates complexity" — the current web is a visual abstraction hiding actual data; the agent browser strips the abstraction and gives you the data directly. | Current browser-use and computer-use approaches prove too fragile or expensive for production agent web interaction; or the wearable/AR system needs a non-visual web consumption layer |
| Agent-native programming language | This session (2026-03-29) | A programming language designed for agents first, not humans first. Sovereign all the way down taken to the language layer. Properties that existing languages lack but agents need: (1) *Natural language interoperability* — optimized for LLM readability/writability; constrained solution space, collocated docs, pipe-first data flow (Elixir scored 97.5% on Autocodebench for these reasons). (2) *Verifiability built in* — mandatory contracts enforced by compiler, not optional type hints; Curry-Howard (proofs = programs) as a language primitive. (3) *Temporal awareness* — facts have timestamps; bi-temporal state (valid/invalid, created/expired) as a language primitive, not a library. (4) *Skill-native* — skills as first-class constructs with rubric, tools, trigger conditions, and body; the compiler knows what a skill is. (5) *OODA-native* — observe/orient/decide/act as language-level constructs; phase transitions are compiler-enforced. (6) *Reversibility as a type* — permanent vs. reversible as a type-system property; compiler prevents permanent actions inside sandboxed contexts. (7) *Low-level clarity* (Fleury) — maps directly to hardware/memory constraints; no hidden abstractions. (8) *Pipe-first data flow* — describe what's happening, not how memory is managed; agents think in data flow. (9) *Sovereign by design* — no external runtime dependencies; compiles to something that runs on our infrastructure. The practical question: would language-level constraints prevent meaningful classes of errors that conventions and linting cannot? If yes, the language earns its existence. | The system is producing enough code that language-level guarantees would prevent meaningful classes of errors that conventions and linting cannot; sovereign model registry is active and could benefit from a language co-designed with the models that write it |
| Making domains verifiable — the decade-long work | This session (2026-03-29) | The work of the next decade across all domains is making the fuzzy verifiable. Once a domain is verifiable, agents can learn in it, benchmark it, automate it, and earn autonomy in it. Fuzzy domains are the last frontier of human-only work. The progression for any domain: (1) **Fuzzy** — no formal criteria, "I know it when I see it," tribal knowledge, vibes. (2) **Partially verifiable** — some criteria formalized, some still judgment. (3) **Verifiable** — clear evaluation criteria, measurable outcomes, agents can learn. (4) **Automated** — agents operate autonomously with earned trust. Every domain in the world is somewhere on this spectrum. Code and math are already verifiable — that's why agents dominate there first. Medicine, law, management, design, strategy, art — all partially fuzzy, all candidates for the push rightward. The work is making each domain's evaluation criteria explicit enough that an agent can be measured against them. This connects to: verifier's law (domain verifiability determines learning capacity), formalization threshold (the moment a pattern becomes formal), bottleneck-targeted benchmarks (can't benchmark what you can't verify), digital garden lifecycle (seed=fuzzy, formalized=verifiable), Orient's role (transforms fuzzy situations into verifiable path statements), automatic curriculum (identifies the next verifiable frontier), sculpting civilizational memory (what you're sculpting IS verifiability), and the agent lab (designs games to make new domains verifiable). The highest-leverage act in any domain is not automating it — it's making it verifiable. Automation follows naturally. | Continuous — this is the overarching thesis; every other deferred entry is an instance of this work |
| Sculpting civilizational memory | This session (2026-03-29) | The system sculpts memory — it doesn't just store information, it intentionally shapes what's preserved, what's compressed, and what's allowed to decay. At small scale this is already happening: the dream state sculpts vision, the knowledge graph sculpts understanding, the skill library sculpts capability, decision traces sculpt precedent, compaction sculpts forgetting, the digital garden sculpts growth. Sovereignty means this sculpted memory belongs to us. Scale the pattern: each org sculpts its domain memory; the primitive whiteboard shares the best across orgs; the agent lab trains sovereign models on the accumulated knowledge — sculpting memory at organizational scale. Scale further: many such networks sharing primitives through the agentic mesh sculpt memory at civilizational scale. The sculpting metaphor is load-bearing: it implies curation, intentionality, aesthetic judgment about what deserves to endure. Not everything is worth remembering. The compaction protocol, the digital garden compost cycle, the formalization threshold — these are all sculpting tools. The system's long-term value is not the code or the models — it's the sculpted memory they operate on. Whoever sculpts the most durable, most retrievable, most compositional memory has the deepest moat. | The system's accumulated memory (knowledge graph, skill library, decision traces, run archives) is mature enough to be recognized as the primary asset; the sculpting metaphor becomes operational when curation quality matters more than accumulation volume |
| OODA game visualization — Stardew Valley-style observability surface | This session (2026-04-04) | A real-time 2D game visualization of the OODA cycle, inspired by gas-town-game-ui (PixiJS pixel-art RPG rendering Gas Town agents as characters) but designed for genuine observability rather than cosmetic theming. Reference: gas-town-game-ui uses PixiJS + React + TypeScript + WebSocket, connecting to the agent orchestrator — characters walk around rooms but the visualization doesn't represent what work is actually being done. Our version must solve that. **Two competing goals:** (1) *Legibility* — glance at the screen and instantly know what phase, what's stuck, what's progressing; (2) *Fidelity* — the visual accurately represents the nature of the work, not just that work is happening. **Right granularity — three layers:** (1) Phase-level environments — 4 distinct visual zones, one per OODA phase, the primary signal; (2) Primitive-type animations within each zone — not unique art per individual protocol/framework/skill/eval, but a visual class per primitive type; (3) Individual primitives are text labels, not art — a character "observing via reflect-protocol" shows the Observe animation + a text label. The phase tells you the cognitive mode; the label tells you the specific primitive. **Phase metaphor candidates — Observe:** Two angles explored: *mining from substrates* (protocols extract from different data sources; effort required; can hit dead rock) vs *observatory with instruments* (scanning, surveying, seeing the whole picture; adjusting lenses). Mining captures the active extraction but misses the synthesis; observatory captures the unified picture but misses the effort. **Recommended: Observatory with multiple instruments** — the character moves between instruments (each instrument = a protocol's data source). The telescope reads git/codebase. The radio dish receives voice input. The specimen jars are inbox items. The map table is the knowledge graph. Snapshot synthesis is the character writing in a logbook at the central desk. Captures: multi-source reading, active but receptive work, producing a unified output (the logbook/snapshot). **Phase metaphor candidates — Orient:** Orient is the schwerpunkt — hardest to visualize. It's sense-making: consuming the snapshot and finding the fastest path. Options explored: *cartography/map-making* (charting a path; terrain = problem space), *alchemy/workshop* (transforming raw observations; frameworks = recipes — could be confused with Act), *war room / strategy table* (studying the map, considering approaches), *lens grinding / optics* (trying different lenses until picture clears — too subtle visually). **Recommended: Cartography table** — the character works with a map that changes based on which framework they apply. They pick up different instruments (frameworks) and the map reshapes — paths appear, others close, terrain simplifies. The output is a marked-up map with a highlighted route (the path statement). Captures: sense-making, environment reduction (R→D→S), the map IS the path statement. **Phase metaphor candidates — Decide:** Decide translates the path into a task DAG. Planning, not exploring, not building. Options: *blueprint drafting* (creating plans for builders; precision; specs), *chess/Go board* (positional play, selecting moves — too abstract), *dispatch office* (assigning work, ordering tasks, managing dependencies), *recipe/cooking prep* (selecting ingredients, writing recipes — doesn't capture DAG). **Recommended: Dispatch board** — the character works at a task board, pulling loop cards from a library rack on the wall (the Loop Library), writing specs on them, pinning them to the board in dependency order, drawing lines between them. When done, the board IS the plan. The dispatch board could be a real interactive element you click into to see the actual task DAG. **Phase metaphor candidates — Act:** Execution. Shadow clones doing work. Most natural for game metaphor. Options: *construction site* (building from specs; multiple workers — misses isolation), *forge/workshop* (crafting artifacts; skill = technique — misses parallel coordination), *fleet/ships* (independent vessels on missions; coming back with artifacts — good for parallel clones, less for showing work), *farm plots* (each clone tends their plot; artifacts grow — maps to digital garden). **Recommended: Workshop compound with isolated workstations** — each shadow clone gets their own bench/station (isolation), working from a spec pinned above it (from Decide's board). Artifacts visually materialize as the clone works. Eval fires as an inspection — a separate character (or same clone with magnifying glass) checking the artifact against a rubric. Failed evals show visible problems on the artifact. Coverage shows as a progress wall — acceptance criteria listed, filling in with green as artifacts satisfy them. **What would actually be helpful to watch (the instrument test):** (1) Phase indicator — which OODA phase is active, immediately visible by color/zone; (2) Clone roster — how many clones active, what each is doing (task label + phase); (3) Coverage progress — acceptance criteria wall filling in real-time; (4) Bottleneck detection — a clone on the same task too long visually shows distress/stalling; (5) Artifact flow — artifacts being produced and flowing to downstream tasks; (6) The hill chart — already in the dream state, naturally visual, shows uphill/downhill per sub-problem. **Room-per-phase model:** the "camera" follows the active phase. When Observe is running, you're in the Observatory. When Act kicks off, the view shifts to the Workshop compound and you watch clones at their stations. **Tech stack:** PixiJS + WebSocket connected to the orchestrator's MCP server. The orchestrator already has SSE streaming (`/api/executions/:id/stream`), execution state in `data/executions/`, and the dashboard infrastructure. **Open design questions:** (1) Whether the room-per-phase model works when phases overlap (Observe might kick off while Act is still running on a previous cycle's tasks); (2) Whether pixel art is the right aesthetic or whether something more diagrammatic (like the hill chart) would be more useful per square inch of screen; (3) Whether the game metaphor helps or hurts — does making it "fun to watch" actually make it harder to read as an instrument?; (4) How much of this is a Visual loop artifact (one-time design) vs a persistent dashboard. **Prototype sequencing:** build Observatory (Observe) + Workshop (Act) rooms first — those two have the clearest visual language and the most observable state. Orient and Decide are faster phases with less to watch in real-time. If those two rooms prove useful, extend. Connects to: cockpit vocabulary (instruments + controls — this is the most literal cockpit), microscope principle (a tool that lets you see structure in something too complex to visualize directly), Visual loop type (#7 in the Library), output modality matches information type (spatial/relational state → diagram/visual). | The orchestrator's execution engine and SSE streaming are operational; the existing Next.js dashboard proves insufficient for understanding what agents are actually doing; or the pilot needs a "leave it running on a second monitor" observability surface |
| Loop layers (sequential refinement passes) | This session | Loops get a `layers: int = 1` parameter (default 1, matching current behavior). `layers > 1` drives sequential refinement: each layer executes the loop's skill against the previous layer's artifact, informed by structured critique from the previous layer's self-eval. The self-eval is the feedback mechanism — it must produce structured failure reasons (which criteria failed, why, what specifically needs revision), not just a quality score. That critique is what differentiates layer N+1 from layer N; without it, layers collapse to repetition. The loop stops early if self-eval clears all criteria before the layer ceiling. Coupled implementation: `layers` parameter + self-eval structured output belong together. **Early exit gate:** when self-eval signals convergence before the layer ceiling — all criteria passing, no remaining failure reasons — remaining layers are skipped. Running layers past convergence wastes execution. Self-eval rubric score is the convergence signal: high score mid-loop means exit, not continue. **Mode collapse prevention:** if all rubric criteria are satisfiable at layer 1, layers:N silently collapses to layers:1 for every input — the architecture declares N layers but always exits after 1. Prevention: at least one rubric criterion must be impossible to satisfy at layer 1, specifically a criterion requiring evidence of improvement over the prior layer ("does this artifact improve on the previous layer's output?" cannot be answered at layer 1). This is the rubric equivalent of entropy regularization — it forces engagement across layers rather than collapsing to the first exit. **Overlooping vs. underlooping asymmetry:** overlooping (declaring more layers than needed) is safe — the early exit gate handles it gracefully. Underlooping (too few layers declared) leaves quality on the table with no recovery mechanism. Planning guidance: when Decide sets layers:N, err high. The exit gate is the floor; there is no ceiling recovery. **Loops as context-extension alternative:** loops don't extend context — they recurse through bounded context. A task requiring a long reasoning chain inside a single call is better served by loop iterations, which keep each pass bounded and reduce drift risk. The longer the required reasoning chain, the stronger the case for loops:N over a single extended pass. | Loop Library is stable and self-eval is implemented; implement together as one unit |

---

### Loop Structural Taxonomy (Deferred)

*Seven structural types from a cross-domain survey of loops (musical, cybernetic, ecological, computational). Classify existing loops by structural type; use when designing new loop types and when Decide reasons about loop behavior beyond artifact type.*

| Type | Canonical example | Key property | System implication |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Fixed loop** | Musical ostinato, game update/render | Identical repetition; period constant | Game loops (update/render) have a fixed period (target frame rate) with adaptive mechanisms to handle overrun — a real-time constraint architecture. When our loops run on a scheduled cadence, the same pattern applies: declare target period, handle overrun gracefully |
| **Feedback loop** | Thermostat, OODA | Output becomes input; gain determines stability | OODA tempo advantage: the side with the shorter loop period gets inside the opponent's loop and generates more decisions per unit time. Speed of iteration is a competitive primitive |
| **Strange loop** | Gödel/Escher/Bach, consciousness (Hofstadter) | A level-crossing loop: following it brings you back to the start but at a higher (or lower) logical level — self-reference creates emergent properties not present in any single level | Meta-loops 8–11 are strange loops; already encoded at "system is its own first customer." Hofstadter's argument: this level-crossing is what produces consciousness. The system's compounding is not legible from any one loop in isolation |
| **Learning loop** | PDCA, double-loop (Argyris) | State mutates; the loop improves itself | Single-loop corrects errors within the existing model; double-loop questions the model itself; triple-loop questions who is doing the questioning. Current loops are single-loop. Meta-loop is the double-loop mechanism. Dream-protocol is triple-loop — the human questions the questioning |
| **Recursive loop** | Factorial, fractals | Self-similar; base case terminates | Loop-within-loop structures throughout the harness; base case = dream state completion (the system's implicit exit condition) |
| **Drift loop** | Tape loops, ecological cycles | Period or content gradually shifts | Musical loops that drift create productive tension — the slight detuning of a tape loop (Eno, Reich) produces emergent complexity from a simple rule. Drift is generative, not error. Learning loops in the harness ARE drift loops by design: quality bar shifts as confidence grows. Dream state is a drift loop across sessions: each vision session intentionally shifts the target state |
| **Nested loop** | Event loop containing game loop | Hierarchy of periods and scopes | Phase coupling in music: two loops phase-locked to a shared tempo vs. free-running. Polyrhythm emerges when loops have non-integer period ratios — phase relationships create structure. Relevant when loop-sequencing composes multi-loop plans |

**Cross-type observations:**
- **Habit loop** (cue → routine → reward) is a feedback loop where the reward strengthens the cue probability — positive gain around the loop; this is how habits become sticky. Explains why `quality_score` makes good skills sticky: high score increases selection probability, increasing invocations, increasing signal — the habit forms at the library level
- **Exit conditions:** most loops don't have them (musical loops play until stopped); the most powerful design choice is making exit conditions explicit and tied to semantic completion. Dream state = implicit exit for the whole system
